0005E3r 3                               ; Increment the tmp3 pointer so we can use ,y addressing
0005E3r 3                               ; on both tmp1 (the input buffer) and tmp3 (the history
0005E3r 3                               ; buffer)
0005E3r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp3
0005E5r 3  D0 02                        bne @2           ; Increment the upper byte on carry.
0005E7r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp3+1
0005E9r 3               @2:
0005E9r 3                               ; Copy the history buffer into the input buffer,
0005E9r 3                               ; sending the characters to the output as we go.
0005E9r 3  A9 0D                        lda #AscCR
0005EBr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
0005EEr 3               
0005EEr 3               @history_loop:
0005EEr 3                               ; See if we have reached the end of the history buffer.
0005EEr 3  C4 rr                        cpy status+1
0005F0r 3  D0 03                        bne @3
0005F2r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp accept_loop       ; Needs a long jump
0005F5r 3               @3:
0005F5r 3                               ; See if we have reached the end of the input buffer.
0005F5r 3                               ; (only comparing to lower byte as we currently limit
0005F5r 3                               ; to 255 characters max)
0005F5r 3  C4 rr                        cpy tmp2
0005F7r 3  F0 0A                        beq @hist_filled_buffer
0005F9r 3               
0005F9r 3                               ; Copy a character and echo.
0005F9r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp3),y
0005FBr 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp1),y
0005FDr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
000600r 3               
000600r 3                               ; Move to the next character.
000600r 3  C8                           iny
000601r 3  80 EB                        bra @history_loop
000603r 3               
000603r 3               @hist_filled_buffer:
000603r 3                               ; We don't want a history recall to EOL our buffer,
000603r 3                               ; so back up one character and return to editing.
000603r 3  88                           dey
000604r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp accept_loop
000607r 3               accept_done:
000607r 3               @done:
000607r 3                               ; Copy the input buffer into the currently
000607r 3                               ; selected history buffer.
000607r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr total_recall
00060Ar 3  85 rr                        sta status+1
00060Cr 3               
00060Cr 3                               ; Also save it in the first buffer byte.
00060Cr 3  A0 00                        ldy #0
00060Er 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp3),y
000610r 3               
000610r 3                               ; Move path the count to the data bytes
000610r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp3
000612r 3  D0 02                        bne @4           ; Increment the upper byte on carry.
000614r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp3+1
000616r 3               @4:
000616r 3                               ; Copy the characters from the input buffer to the
000616r 3                               ; history buffer.
000616r 3               
000616r 3               @save_history_loop:
000616r 3  C4 rr                        cpy status+1
000618r 3  F0 07                        beq @save_history_done
00061Ar 3               
00061Ar 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
00061Cr 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp3),y
00061Er 3  C8                           iny
00061Fr 3  80 F5                        bra @save_history_loop
000621r 3               
000621r 3               @save_history_done:
000621r 3               z_accept:
000621r 3  60                           rts
000622r 3               
000622r 3               total_recall:
000622r 3                       ; """Internal subroutine for ACCEPT that recalls history entry"""
000622r 3               
000622r 3                               ; Generate the address of the buffer in tmp3. Start with the
000622r 3                               ; base address.
000622r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<hist_buff
000624r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3
000626r 3  A9 rr                        lda #>hist_buff
000628r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3+1
00062Ar 3               
00062Ar 3                               ; This is a bit annoying as some bits go into each byte.
00062Ar 3                               ; .....xxx gets put into address like ......xx x.......
00062Ar 3  A5 rr                        lda status
00062Cr 3  6A                           ror
00062Dr 3  29 03                        and #3
00062Fr 3  18                           clc
000630r 3  65 rr                        adc tmp3+1
000632r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3+1
000634r 3               
000634r 3  A5 rr                        lda status
000636r 3  6A                           ror             ; Rotate through carry into msb.
000637r 3  6A                           ror
000638r 3  29 80                        and #$80
00063Ar 3  18                           clc
00063Br 3  65 rr                        adc tmp3
00063Dr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3
00063Fr 3  90 02                        bcc @1           ; Increment the upper byte on carry.
000641r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp3+1
000643r 3               @1:
000643r 3                               ; Save the current length of the input buffer in
000643r 3                               ; histinfo+1 temporarily.  Reduce to 127 if larger.
000643r 3  98                           tya
000644r 3  C9 80                        cmp #$80
000646r 3  90 02                        bcc @2
000648r 3  A9 7F                        lda #$7F
00064Ar 3               @2:
00064Ar 3  60                           rts
00064Br 3               
00064Br 3               
00064Br 3               
00064Br 3               
00064Br 3               
00064Br 3               ; ## ACTION_OF ( "name" -- xt ) "Get named deferred word's xt"
00064Br 3               ; ## "action-of"  auto  ANS core ext
00064Br 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ACTION-OF"""
00064Br 3               
00064Br 3               xt_action_of:
00064Br 3                               ; This is a state aware word with differet behavior
00064Br 3                               ; when used while compiling vs interpreting.
00064Br 3                               ; Check STATE
00064Br 3  A5 rr                        lda state
00064Dr 3  05 rr                        ora state+1
00064Fr 3  F0 0C                        beq @interpreting
000651r 3               
000651r 3               @compiling:
000651r 3                               ; Run ['] to compile the xt of the next word
000651r 3                               ; as a literal.
000651r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_bracket_tick
000654r 3               
000654r 3                               ; Postpone DEFER@ by compiling a JSR to it.
000654r 3  A0 rr                        ldy #>xt_defer_fetch
000656r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<xt_defer_fetch
000658r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_subroutine
00065Br 3  80 06                        bra @done
00065Dr 3               
00065Dr 3               @interpreting:
00065Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_tick
000660r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_defer_fetch
000663r 3               
000663r 3               @done:
000663r 3  60           z_action_of:           rts
000664r 3               
000664r 3               
000664r 3               
000664r 3               ; ## AGAIN ( addr -- ) "Code backwards branch to address left by BEGIN"
000664r 3               ; ## "again"  tested  ANS core ext
000664r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/AGAIN"""
000664r 3               
000664r 3               xt_again:
000664r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
000667r 3               
000667r 3                               ; Add the opcode for a JMP. We use JMP instead of BRA
000667r 3                               ; so we have the range and don't have to calculate the
000667r 3                               ; offset.
000667r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0
000669r 3  A9 4C                        lda #$4C        ; JMP
00066Br 3  91 rr                        sta (cp),y
00066Dr 3  C8                           iny
00066Er 3               
00066Er 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x         ; LSB of address
000670r 3  91 rr                        sta (cp),y
000672r 3  C8                           iny
000673r 3               
000673r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x         ; MSB of address
000675r 3  91 rr                        sta (cp),y
000677r 3  C8                           iny
000678r 3               
000678r 3                               ; Allot the space we just used
000678r 3  98                           tya
000679r 3  18                           clc
00067Ar 3  65 rr                        adc cp
00067Cr 3  85 rr                        sta cp
00067Er 3  90 02                        bcc @done
000680r 3  E6 rr                        inc cp+1
000682r 3               @done:
000682r 3  E8                           inx
000683r 3  E8                           inx
000684r 3               
000684r 3  60           z_again:        rts
000685r 3               
000685r 3               
000685r 3               
000685r 3               ; ## ALIGN ( -- ) "Make sure CP is aligned on word size"
000685r 3               ; ## "align"  auto  ANS core
000685r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ALIGN
000685r 3                       ; On a 8-bit machine, this does nothing. ALIGNED uses this
000685r 3                       ; routine as well, and also does nothing
000685r 3                       ; """
000685r 3               
000685r 3               ; ## ALIGNED ( addr -- addr ) "Return the first aligned address"
000685r 3               ; ## "aligned"  auto  ANS core
000685r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ALIGNED"""
000685r 3               
000685r 3               xt_align:
000685r 3               xt_aligned:
000685r 3               z_align:
000685r 3  60           z_aligned:      rts             ; stripped out during native compile
000686r 3               
000686r 3               
000686r 3               
000686r 3               ; ## ALLOT ( n -- ) "Reserve or release memory"
000686r 3               ; ## "allot"  auto  ANS core
000686r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ALLOT
000686r 3                       ; Reserve a certain number of bytes (not cells) or release them.
000686r 3                       ; If n = 0, do nothing. If n is negative, release n bytes, but only
000686r 3                       ; to the beginning of the Dictionary. If n is positive (the most
000686r 3                       ; common case), reserve n bytes, but not past the end of the
000686r 3                       ; Dictionary. See http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ALLOT
000686r 3                       ; """
000686r 3               
000686r 3               xt_allot:
000686r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
000689r 3               
000689r 3                               ; Releasing memory is going to be a very rare operation,
000689r 3                               ; so we check for it at the beginning and try to make
000689r 3                               ; the most common case as fast as possible
000689r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
00068Br 3  30 22                        bmi @release
00068Dr 3               
00068Dr 3                               ; Common case: We are reserving memory, not releasing it
00068Dr 3  18                           clc
00068Er 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
000690r 3  75 00                        adc 0,x
000692r 3  85 rr                        sta cp
000694r 3               
000694r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
000696r 3  75 01                        adc 1,x
000698r 3  85 rr                        sta cp+1
00069Ar 3               
00069Ar 3                               ; Wait, did we just grant more space than we have? This is
00069Ar 3                               ; a check we only do here, not for other situations like cmpl_a
00069Ar 3                               ; where smaller amounts are reserved.
00069Ar 3  A0 FF                        ldy #<cp_end
00069Cr 3  C4 rr                        cpy cp
00069Er 3  A9 7F                        lda #>cp_end
0006A0r 3  E5 rr                        sbc cp+1
0006A2r 3  B0 48                        bcs @done               ; we're fine.
0006A4r 3               
0006A4r 3                               ; Oops, that was too much, we're beyond the end of
0006A4r 3                               ; legal Dictionary RAM. Reduce to max memory and report
0006A4r 3                               ; an error
0006A4r 3  84 rr                        sty cp                  ; still #<cp_end
0006A6r 3  A9 7F                        lda #>cp_end
0006A8r 3  85 rr                        sta cp+1
0006AAr 3               
0006AAr 3  A9 00                        lda #err_allot
0006ACr 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
0006AFr 3               
0006AFr 3               @release:
0006AFr 3                  		; The ANS standard doesn't really say what to do if too much
0006AFr 3                               ; memory is freed ("negatively alloted"). In fact, there isn't
0006AFr 3                               ; even an official test. Gforth is little help either. The good
0006AFr 3                               ; news is, this is going to be a rare case. We want to use as
0006AFr 3                               ; few bytes as possible.
0006AFr 3               
0006AFr 3                               ; What we do is let the user free anything up to the beginning
0006AFr 3                               ; of the RAM area assigned to the Dicionary (CP0), but at
0006AFr 3                               ; their own risk. This means that the Dictionary pointer DP
0006AFr 3                               ; might end up pointing to garbage. However, an attempt to
0006AFr 3                               ; free more than RAM than CP0 will lead to CP being set to CP0,
0006AFr 3                               ; the DP pointing to the last word in RAM (should be DROP) and
0006AFr 3                               ; an error message.
0006AFr 3               
0006AFr 3                               ; We arrive here with ( n ) which is negative. First step,
0006AFr 3                               ; subtract the number TOS from the CP for a new CP
0006AFr 3  CA                           dex
0006B0r 3  CA                           dex
0006B1r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
0006B3r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0006B5r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
0006B7r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
0006B9r 3               
0006B9r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_plus                     ; new CP is now TOS
0006BCr 3               
0006BCr 3                               ; Second step, see if we've gone too far. We compare the new
0006BCr 3                               ; CP on TOS (which, if we've really screwed up, might be
0006BCr 3                               ; negative) with CP0. This is a signed comparison
0006BCr 3  CA                           dex
0006BDr 3  CA                           dex                             ; new CP now NOS
0006BEr 3  A9 rr                        lda #<cp0
0006C0r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0006C2r 3  A9 rr                        lda #>cp0
0006C4r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x                         ; CP0 is TOS
0006C6r 3               
0006C6r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr compare_16bit               ; still ( CP CP0 )
0006C9r 3               
0006C9r 3                               ; If CP (NOS) is smaller than CP0 (TOS), we're in trouble.
0006C9r 3                               ; This means we want Z=1 or N=1
0006C9r 3  F0 17                        beq @nega_done
0006CBr 3  30 15                        bmi @nega_done
0006CDr 3               
0006CDr 3                               ; Yep, we're in trouble. Set CP to CP0, set DP to the first
0006CDr 3                               ; word in ROM (should be DROP), and abort with an error
0006CDr 3  A9 rr                        lda #<cp0
0006CFr 3  85 rr                        sta cp
0006D1r 3  A9 rr                        lda #>cp0
0006D3r 3  85 rr                        sta cp+1
0006D5r 3               
0006D5r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<dictionary_start
0006D7r 3  85 rr                        sta dp
0006D9r 3  A9 rr                        lda #>dictionary_start
0006DBr 3  85 rr                        sta dp+1
0006DDr 3               
0006DDr 3  A9 0A                        lda #err_negallot
0006DFr 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
0006E2r 3               
0006E2r 3               @nega_done:
0006E2r 3                               ; Save new CP, which is NOS
0006E2r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
0006E4r 3  85 rr                        sta cp
0006E6r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0006E8r 3  85 rr                        sta cp+1
0006EAr 3               
0006EAr 3  E8                           inx
0006EBr 3  E8                           inx                     ; drop through to @done
0006ECr 3               @done:
0006ECr 3  E8                           inx
0006EDr 3  E8                           inx
0006EEr 3               z_allot:
0006EEr 3  60                           rts
0006EFr 3               
0006EFr 3               
0006EFr 3               
0006EFr 3               ; ## ALLOW_NATIVE ( -- ) "Flag last word to allow native compiling"
0006EFr 3               ; ## "allow-native"  auto  Tali Forth
0006EFr 3               xt_allow_native:
0006EFr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr current_to_dp
0006F2r 3  A0 01                        ldy #1          ; offset for status byte
0006F4r 3  B1 rr                        lda (dp),y
0006F6r 3  29 F5                        and #$ff-NN-AN  ; AN and NN flag is clear.
0006F8r 3  91 rr                        sta (dp),y
0006FAr 3               z_allow_native:
0006FAr 3  60                           rts
0006FBr 3               
0006FBr 3               
0006FBr 3               ; ## ALSO ( -- ) "Make room in the search order for another wordlist"
0006FBr 3               ; ## "also"  auto  ANS search ext
0006FBr 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/search/ALSO"""
0006FBr 3               xt_also:
0006FBr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_get_order
0006FEr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_over
000701r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_swap
000704r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_one_plus
000707r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_set_order
00070Ar 3               
00070Ar 3  60           z_also:         rts
00070Br 3               
00070Br 3               
00070Br 3               ; ## ALWAYS_NATIVE ( -- ) "Flag last word as always natively compiled"
00070Br 3               ; ## "always-native"  auto  Tali Forth
00070Br 3               xt_always_native:
00070Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr current_to_dp
00070Er 3  A0 01                        ldy #1          ; offset for status byte
000710r 3  B1 rr                        lda (dp),y
000712r 3  09 02                        ora #AN         ; Make sure AN flag is set
000714r 3  29 F7                        and #$ff-NN     ; and NN flag is clear.
000716r 3  91 rr                        sta (dp),y
000718r 3               z_always_native:
000718r 3  60                           rts
000719r 3               
000719r 3               
000719r 3               ; ## AND ( n n -- n ) "Logically AND TOS and NOS"
000719r 3               ; ## "and"  auto  ANS core
000719r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/AND"""
000719r 3               xt_and:
000719r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
00071Cr 3               
00071Cr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
00071Er 3  35 02                        and 2,x
000720r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
000722r 3               
000722r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
000724r 3  35 03                        and 3,x
000726r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
000728r 3               
000728r 3  E8                           inx
000729r 3  E8                           inx
00072Ar 3               
00072Ar 3  60           z_and:          rts
00072Br 3               
00072Br 3               
00072Br 3               ; ## ASSEMBLER_WORDLIST ( -- u ) "WID for the Assembler wordlist"
00072Br 3               ; ## "assembler-wordlist"  tested  Tali Assembler
00072Br 3                       ; """ Commonly used like `assembler-wordlist >order` to add the
00072Br 3                       ; assembler words to the search order so they can be used.
00072Br 3                       ; See the tutorial on Wordlists and the Search Order for
00072Br 3                       ; more information.
00072Br 3                       ;
00072Br 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the code is shared with TWO
00072Br 3                       ; """
00072Br 3               
00072Br 3               
00072Br 3               ; ## AT_XY ( n m -- ) "Move cursor to position given"
00072Br 3               ; ## "at-xy"  tested  ANS facility
00072Br 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/facility/AT-XY
00072Br 3                       ; On an ANSI compatible terminal, place cursor at row n colum m.
00072Br 3                       ; ANSI code is ESC[<n>;<m>H
00072Br 3                       ;
00072Br 3                       ; Do not use U. to print the numbers because the
00072Br 3                       ; trailing space will not work with xterm
00072Br 3                       ; """
00072Br 3               xt_at_xy:
00072Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
00072Er 3               
00072Er 3  A9 1B                        lda #AscESC
000730r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
000733r 3  A9 5B                        lda #$5B        ; ASCII for "["
000735r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
000738r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_u
00073Br 3  A9 3B                        lda #$3B        ; ASCII for ";"
00073Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
000740r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_u
000743r 3  A9 48                        lda #'H'
000745r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
000748r 3               
000748r 3  60           z_at_xy:        rts
000749r 3               
000749r 3               
000749r 3               ; ## BACKSLASH ( -- ) "Ignore rest of line"
000749r 3               ; ## "\"  auto  ANS core ext
000749r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/bs"""
000749r 3               xt_backslash:
000749r 3  A5 rr                        lda ciblen
00074Br 3  85 rr                        sta toin
00074Dr 3  A5 rr                        lda ciblen+1
00074Fr 3  85 rr                        sta toin+1
000751r 3               
000751r 3  60           z_backslash:    rts
000752r 3               
000752r 3               
000752r 3               ; ## BASE ( -- addr ) "Push address of radix base to stack"
000752r 3               ; ## "base"  auto  ANS core
000752r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BASE
000752r 3                       ; The ANS Forth standard sees the base up to 36, so we can cheat and
000752r 3                       ; ingore the MSB
000752r 3                       ; """
000752r 3               xt_base:
000752r 3  CA                           dex
000753r 3  CA                           dex
000754r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<base
000756r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x         ; LSB
000758r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; MSB is always 0
00075Ar 3               
00075Ar 3  60           z_base:         rts
00075Br 3               
00075Br 3               
00075Br 3               ; ## BEGIN ( -- addr ) "Mark entry point for loop"
00075Br 3               ; ## "begin"  auto  ANS core
00075Br 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BEGIN
00075Br 3                       ;
00075Br 3                       ; This is just an immediate version of here which could just
00075Br 3                       ; as well be coded in Forth as
00075Br 3                       ;       : BEGIN HERE ; IMMEDIATE COMPILE-ONLY
00075Br 3                       ; Since this is a compiling word, we don't care that much about
00075Br 3                       ; about speed
00075Br 3                       ; """
00075Br 3               
00075Br 3               xt_begin:
00075Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_here
00075Er 3  60           z_begin:        rts
00075Fr 3               
00075Fr 3               
00075Fr 3               
00075Fr 3               ; ## BELL ( -- ) "Emit ASCII BELL"
00075Fr 3               ; ## "bell"  tested  Tali Forth
00075Fr 3               xt_bell:
00075Fr 3  A9 07                        lda #7          ; ASCII value for BELl
000761r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
000764r 3               
000764r 3  60           z_bell:         rts
000765r 3               
000765r 3               
000765r 3               ; ## BL ( -- c ) "Push ASCII value of SPACE to stack"
000765r 3               ; ## "bl"  auto  ANS core
000765r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BL"""
000765r 3               
000765r 3               xt_bl:
000765r 3  CA                           dex
000766r 3  CA                           dex
000767r 3  A9 20                        lda #AscSP
000769r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00076Br 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
00076Dr 3               
00076Dr 3  60           z_bl:           rts
00076Er 3               
00076Er 3               
00076Er 3               ; ## BLK ( -- addr ) "Push address of block being interpreted"
00076Er 3               ; ## "block"  auto  ANS block
00076Er 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/BLK"""
00076Er 3               xt_blk:
00076Er 3                               ; BLK is at UP + blk_offset
00076Er 3  CA                           dex
00076Fr 3  CA                           dex
000770r 3  18                           clc
000771r 3  A5 rr                        lda up
000773r 3  69 00                        adc #blk_offset ; Add offset
000775r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
000777r 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
000779r 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; Adding carry
00077Br 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
00077Dr 3               
00077Dr 3  60           z_blk:          rts
00077Er 3               
00077Er 3               
00077Er 3               ; ## BLKBUFFER ( -- addr ) "Push address of block buffer"
00077Er 3               ; ## "blkbuffer"  auto  Tali block
00077Er 3               xt_blkbuffer:
00077Er 3                               ; blkbuffer address is at UP + blkbuffer_offset.
00077Er 3                               ; Unlike some of the other user variables, we actually
00077Er 3                               ; want to push the address stored here, which will
00077Er 3                               ; point to somewhere outside of the user variables.
00077Er 3  CA                           dex
00077Fr 3  CA                           dex
000780r 3                               ; Put the address on the stack.
000780r 3  A0 28                        ldy #blkbuffer_offset
000782r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000784r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
000786r 3  C8                           iny             ; Move along to the next byte
000787r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000789r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
00078Br 3               
00078Br 3  60           z_blkbuffer:    rts
00078Cr 3               
00078Cr 3               
00078Cr 3               ; ## BLOCK ( u -- a-addr ) "Fetch a block into a buffer"
00078Cr 3               ; ## "block"  auto  ANS block
00078Cr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/BLOCK"""
00078Cr 3               
00078Cr 3               xt_block:
00078Cr 3               
00078Cr 3                               ; See if the block requested is the same as the one we
00078Cr 3                               ; currently have in the buffer. Check the LSB.
00078Cr 3  A0 2A                        ldy #buffblocknum_offset
00078Er 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000790r 3  D5 00                        cmp 0,x
000792r 3  D0 0F                        bne @not_in_buffer
000794r 3               
000794r 3                               ; Check the MSB.
000794r 3  C8                           iny
000795r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000797r 3  D5 01                        cmp 1,x
000799r 3  D0 08                        bne @not_in_buffer
00079Br 3               
00079Br 3                               ; The block is in the buffer. See if the buffer is in use.
00079Br 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
00079Dr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00079Fr 3  29 01                        and #1          ; Check the in-use flag (bit 0)
0007A1r 3  D0 30                        bne @done       ; It's already in the buffer and in use.
0007A3r 3                                               ; @done will replace the block# with the
0007A3r 3                                               ; buffer address.
0007A3r 3               @not_in_buffer:
0007A3r 3                               ; Check the buffer status
0007A3r 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
0007A5r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y      ; Only bits 0 and 1 are used, so only
0007A7r 3  C9 03                        cmp #3          ; LSB is needed.
0007A9r 3  D0 0C                        bne @buffer_available ; Unused or not dirty = available
0007ABr 3               
0007ABr 3                               ; We need to save the block.
0007ABr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_blkbuffer
0007AEr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_buffblocknum
0007B1r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_fetch
0007B4r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_block_write
0007B7r 3               
0007B7r 3               @buffer_available:
0007B7r 3                               ; Save the block number.
0007B7r 3  A0 2A                        ldy #buffblocknum_offset
0007B9r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0007BBr 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0007BDr 3  C8                           iny
0007BEr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
0007C0r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0007C2r 3               
0007C2r 3                               ; Get the requested block.
0007C2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_blkbuffer
0007C5r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_swap
0007C8r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_block_read
0007CBr 3               
0007CBr 3                               ; Mark the buffer as clean and in-use.
0007CBr 3  A9 01                        lda #1
0007CDr 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
0007CFr 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0007D1r 3               
0007D1r 3                               ; Make room on the stack for the return address.
0007D1r 3  CA                           dex
0007D2r 3  CA                           dex
0007D3r 3               
0007D3r 3               @done:
0007D3r 3                               ; It's in the buffer. Return the buffer address.
0007D3r 3  A0 28                        ldy #blkbuffer_offset
0007D5r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0007D7r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0007D9r 3  C8                           iny
0007DAr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0007DCr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
0007DEr 3               
0007DEr 3  60           z_block:        rts
0007DFr 3               
0007DFr 3               
0007DFr 3               
0007DFr 3               ; ## BLOCK_RAMDRIVE_INIT ( u -- ) "Create a ramdrive for blocks"
0007DFr 3               ; ## "block-ramdrive-init"  auto  Tali block
0007DFr 3                       ; """Create a RAM drive, with the given number of
0007DFr 3                       ; blocks, in the dictionary along with setting up the block words to
0007DFr 3                       ; use it.  The read/write routines do not provide bounds checking.
0007DFr 3                       ; Expected use: `4 block-ramdrive-init` ( to create blocks 0-3 )
0007DFr 3                       ; """
0007DFr 3               
0007DFr 3               xt_block_ramdrive_init:
0007DFr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0007E2r 3               
0007E2r 3                               ; Store the string to run here as a string literal.
0007E2r 3                               ; See SLITERAL for the format information. This way, we
0007E2r 3                               ; don't have the words defined below in the Dictionary until
0007E2r 3                               ; we really use them.
0007E2r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @after_ramdrive_code
0007E5r 3               
0007E5r 3               @ramdrive_code:
0007E5r 3  62 61 73 65          .byte "base @ swap decimal"
0007E9r 3  20 40 20 73  
0007EDr 3  77 61 70 20  
0007F8r 3  20 31 30 32          .byte " 1024 *" ; ( Calculate how many bytes are needed for numblocks blocks )
0007FCr 3  34 20 2A     
0007FFr 3  20 64 75 70          .byte " dup"    ; ( Save a copy for formatting it at the end )
000803r 3  20 62 75 66          .byte " buffer: ramdrive" ; ( Create ramdrive )
000807r 3  66 65 72 3A  
00080Br 3  20 72 61 6D  
000814r 3                       ; ( These routines just copy between the buffer and the ramdrive blocks )
000814r 3  20 3A 20 62          .byte " : block-read-ramdrive"  ; ( addr u -- )
000818r 3  6C 6F 63 6B  
00081Cr 3  2D 72 65 61  
00082Ar 3  20 72 61 6D          .byte " ramdrive swap 1024 * + swap 1024 move ;"
00082Er 3  64 72 69 76  
000832r 3  65 20 73 77  
000852r 3  20 3A 20 62          .byte " : block-write-ramdrive" ; ( addr u -- )
000856r 3  6C 6F 63 6B  
00085Ar 3  2D 77 72 69  
000869r 3  20 72 61 6D          .byte " ramdrive swap 1024 * + 1024 move ;"
00086Dr 3  64 72 69 76  
000871r 3  65 20 73 77  
00088Cr 3  20 27 20 62          .byte " ' block-read-ramdrive block-read-vector !" ; ( Replace I/O vectors )
000890r 3  6C 6F 63 6B  
000894r 3  2D 72 65 61  
0008B6r 3  20 27 20 62          .byte " ' block-write-ramdrive block-write-vector !"
0008BAr 3  6C 6F 63 6B  
0008BEr 3  2D 77 72 69  
0008E2r 3  20 72 61 6D          .byte " ramdrive swap blank base !"
0008E6r 3  64 72 69 76  
0008EAr 3  65 20 73 77  
0008FDr 3               
0008FDr 3               @after_ramdrive_code:
0008FDr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr sliteral_runtime
000900r 3               
000900r 3  rr rr 18 01  .word @ramdrive_code, @after_ramdrive_code-@ramdrive_code
000904r 3               
000904r 3                               ; The address and length of the ramdrive code is now on the
000904r 3                               ; stack. Call EVALUATE to run it.
000904r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_evaluate
000907r 3               
000907r 3               z_block_ramdrive_init:
000907r 3  60                           rts
000908r 3               
000908r 3               
000908r 3               
000908r 3               ; ## BLOCK_READ ( addr u -- ) "Read a block from storage (deferred word)"
000908r 3               ; ## "block-read"  auto  Tali block
000908r 3                       ; """BLOCK-READ is a vectored word that the user needs to override
000908r 3                       ; with their own version to read a block from storage.
000908r 3                       ; The stack parameters are ( buffer_address block# -- ).
000908r 3                       ; """
000908r 3               xt_block_read:
000908r 3                               ; Execute the BLOCK-READ-VECTOR
000908r 3  A0 2E                        ldy #blockread_offset
00090Ar 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00090Cr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00090Er 3  C8                           iny
00090Fr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000911r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
000913r 3               
000913r 3  6C rr rr                     jmp (tmp1)
000916r 3               
000916r 3               z_block_read:   ; No RTS needed
000916r 3               
000916r 3               
000916r 3               ; ## BLOCK_READ_VECTOR ( -- addr ) "Address of the block-read vector"
000916r 3               ; ## "block-read-vector"  auto  Tali block
000916r 3                       ; """BLOCK-READ is a vectored word that the user needs to override
000916r 3                       ; with their own version to read a block from storage.
000916r 3                       ; This word gives the address of the vector so it can be replaced.
000916r 3                       ; """
000916r 3               xt_block_read_vector:
000916r 3                               ; Get the BLOCK-READ-VECTOR address
000916r 3  CA                           dex
000917r 3  CA                           dex
000918r 3  18                           clc
000919r 3  A5 rr                        lda up
00091Br 3  69 2E                        adc #blockread_offset
00091Dr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00091Fr 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
000921r 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; Add carry
000923r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
000925r 3               
000925r 3               z_block_read_vector:
000925r 3  60                           rts
000926r 3               
000926r 3               
000926r 3               ; This is the default error message the vectored words BLOCK-READ and
000926r 3               ; BLOCK-WRITE start with. This word is not included in the dictionary.
000926r 3               xt_block_word_error:
000926r 3  A9 0C                        lda #err_blockwords
000928r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error       ; no RTS needed
00092Br 3               z_block_word_error:
00092Br 3               
00092Br 3               ; ## BLOCK_WRITE ( addr u -- ) "Write a block to storage (deferred word)"
00092Br 3               ; ## "block-write"  auto  Tali block
00092Br 3                       ; """BLOCK-WRITE is a vectored word that the user needs to override
00092Br 3                       ; with their own version to write a block to storage.
00092Br 3                       ; The stack parameters are ( buffer_address block# -- ).
00092Br 3                       ; """
00092Br 3               xt_block_write:
00092Br 3                               ; Execute the BLOCK-READ-VECTOR
00092Br 3  A0 30                        ldy #blockwrite_offset
00092Dr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00092Fr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
000931r 3  C8                           iny
000932r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000934r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
000936r 3  6C rr rr                     jmp (tmp1)
000939r 3               
000939r 3               z_block_write:  ; No RTS needed
000939r 3               
000939r 3               
000939r 3               ; ## BLOCK_WRITE_VECTOR ( -- addr ) "Address of the block-write vector"
000939r 3               ; ## "block-write-vector"  auto  Tali block
000939r 3                       ; """BLOCK-WRITE is a vectored word that the user needs to override
000939r 3                       ; with their own version to write a block to storage.
000939r 3                       ; This word gives the address of the vector so it can be replaced.
000939r 3                       ; """
000939r 3               xt_block_write_vector:
000939r 3                               ; Get the BLOCK-WRITE-VECTOR address
000939r 3  CA                           dex
00093Ar 3  CA                           dex
00093Br 3  18                           clc
00093Cr 3  A5 rr                        lda up
00093Er 3  69 30                        adc #blockwrite_offset
000940r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
000942r 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
000944r 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; Add carry
000946r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
000948r 3               
000948r 3               z_block_write_vector:
000948r 3  60                           rts
000949r 3               
000949r 3               
000949r 3               ; ## BOUNDS ( addr u -- addr+u addr ) "Prepare address for looping"
000949r 3               ; ## "bounds"  auto  Gforth
000949r 3                       ; """http://www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/Memory-Blocks.html
000949r 3                       ; Given a string, return the correct Data Stack parameters for
000949r 3                       ; a DO/LOOP loop over its characters. This is realized as
000949r 3                       ; OVER + SWAP in Forth, but we do it a lot faster in assembler
000949r 3                       ; """
000949r 3               xt_bounds:
000949r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
00094Cr 3               
00094Cr 3  18                           clc
00094Dr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x                 ; LSB u
00094Fr 3  B4 02                        ldy 2,x                 ; LSB addr
000951r 3  75 02                        adc 2,x
000953r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x                 ; LSB addr+u
000955r 3  94 00                        sty 0,x
000957r 3               
000957r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x                 ; MSB u
000959r 3  B4 03                        ldy 3,x                 ; MSB addr
00095Br 3  75 03                        adc 3,x
00095Dr 3  95 03                        sta 3,x                 ; MSB addr+u
00095Fr 3  94 01                        sty 1,x
000961r 3               
000961r 3  60           z_bounds:       rts
000962r 3               
000962r 3               
000962r 3               ; ## BRACKET_CHAR ( "c" -- ) "Compile character"
000962r 3               ; ## "[char]"  auto  ANS core
000962r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BracketCHAR
000962r 3                       ; Compile the ASCII value of a character as a literal. This is an
000962r 3                       ; immediate, compile-only word.
000962r 3                       ;
000962r 3                       ; A definition given in
000962r 3                       ; http://forth-standard.org/standard/implement is
000962r 3                       ; : [CHAR]  CHAR POSTPONE LITERAL ; IMMEDIATE
000962r 3                       ; """
000962r 3               xt_bracket_char:
000962r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_char
000965r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_literal
000968r 3  60           z_bracket_char: rts
000969r 3               
000969r 3               
000969r 3               ; ## BRACKET_TICK ( -- ) "Store xt of following word during compilation"
000969r 3               ; ## "[']"  auto  ANS core
000969r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BracketTick"""
000969r 3               xt_bracket_tick:
000969r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_tick
00096Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_literal
00096Fr 3  60           z_bracket_tick: rts
000970r 3               
000970r 3               
000970r 3               ; ## BUFFBLOCKNUM ( -- addr ) "Push address of variable holding block in buffer"
000970r 3               ; ## "buffblocknum"  auto  Tali block
000970r 3               xt_buffblocknum:
000970r 3                               ; BUFFBLOCKNUM is at UP + buffblocknum_offset
000970r 3  CA                           dex
000971r 3  CA                           dex
000972r 3  18                           clc
000973r 3  A5 rr                        lda up
000975r 3  69 2A                        adc #buffblocknum_offset        ; Add offset
000977r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
000979r 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
00097Br 3  69 00                        adc #0                          ; Adding carry
00097Dr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
00097Fr 3               
00097Fr 3  60           z_buffblocknum: rts
000980r 3               
000980r 3               
000980r 3               ; ## BUFFER ( u -- a-addr ) "Get a buffer for a block"
000980r 3               ; ## "buffer"  auto  ANS block
000980r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/BUFFER"""
000980r 3               
000980r 3               xt_buffer:
000980r 3                               ; Check the buffer status
000980r 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
000982r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y      ; Only bits 0 and 1 are used, so only
000984r 3  C9 03                        cmp #3          ; LSB is needed.
000986r 3  D0 0C                        bne @buffer_available ; Unused or not dirty = available
000988r 3               
000988r 3                               ; We need to save the block.
000988r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_blkbuffer
00098Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_buffblocknum
00098Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_fetch
000991r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_block_write
000994r 3               
000994r 3               @buffer_available:
000994r 3                               ; Save the block number.
000994r 3  A0 2A                        ldy #buffblocknum_offset
000996r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000998r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
00099Ar 3  C8                           iny
00099Br 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
00099Dr 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
00099Fr 3               
00099Fr 3                               ; Mark the buffer as clean and in-use.
00099Fr 3  A9 01                        lda #1
0009A1r 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
0009A3r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0009A5r 3               
0009A5r 3               @done:
0009A5r 3                               ; Return the buffer address.
0009A5r 3  A0 28                        ldy #blkbuffer_offset
0009A7r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0009A9r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0009ABr 3  C8                           iny
0009ACr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0009AEr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
0009B0r 3               
0009B0r 3  60           z_buffer:       rts
0009B1r 3               
0009B1r 3               
0009B1r 3               
0009B1r 3               ; ## BUFFER_COLON ( u "<name>" -- ; -- addr ) "Create an uninitialized buffer"
0009B1r 3               ; ## "buffer:"  auto  ANS core ext
0009B1r 3                               ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BUFFERColon
0009B1r 3                               ; Create a buffer of size u that puts its address on the stack
0009B1r 3                               ; when its name is used.
0009B1r 3                               ; """
0009B1r 3               xt_buffer_colon:
0009B1r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_create
0009B4r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_allot
0009B7r 3  60           z_buffer_colon: rts
0009B8r 3               
0009B8r 3               
0009B8r 3               ; ## BUFFSTATUS ( -- addr ) "Push address of variable holding buffer status"
0009B8r 3               ; ## "buffstatus"  auto  Tali block
0009B8r 3               xt_buffstatus:
0009B8r 3                               ; BUFFSTATUS is at UP + buffstatus_offset
0009B8r 3  CA                           dex
0009B9r 3  CA                           dex
0009BAr 3  18                           clc
0009BBr 3  A5 rr                        lda up
0009BDr 3  69 2C                        adc #buffstatus_offset  ; Add offset
0009BFr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0009C1r 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
0009C3r 3  69 00                        adc #0                  ; Adding carry
0009C5r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
0009C7r 3               
0009C7r 3  60           z_buffstatus:   rts
0009C8r 3               
0009C8r 3               
0009C8r 3               ; ## BYE ( -- ) "Break"
0009C8r 3               ; ## "bye"  tested  ANS tools ext
0009C8r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/tools/BYE"""
0009C8r 3               
0009C8r 3               xt_bye:
0009C8r 3                               ;brk
0009C8r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp platform_bye
0009CBr 3               z_bye:          ;rts             ; never reached
0009CBr 3               
0009CBr 3               
0009CBr 3               
0009CBr 3               ; ## C_COMMA ( c -- ) "Store one byte/char in the Dictionary"
0009CBr 3               ; ## "c,"  auto  ANS core
0009CBr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CComma"""
0009CBr 3               
0009CBr 3               xt_c_comma:
0009CBr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0009CEr 3               
0009CEr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0009D0r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_a
0009D3r 3               
0009D3r 3  E8                           inx
0009D4r 3  E8                           inx
0009D5r 3               
0009D5r 3  60           z_c_comma:      rts
0009D6r 3               
0009D6r 3               
0009D6r 3               
0009D6r 3               ; ## C_FETCH ( addr -- c ) "Get a character/byte from given address"
0009D6r 3               ; ## "c@"  auto  ANS core
0009D6r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CFetch"""
0009D6r 3               xt_c_fetch:
0009D6r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0009D9r 3               
0009D9r 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)
0009DBr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0009DDr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; Ignore LSB
0009DFr 3               
0009DFr 3  60           z_c_fetch:      rts
0009E0r 3               
0009E0r 3               
0009E0r 3               ; ## C_STORE ( c addr -- ) "Store character at address given"
0009E0r 3               ; ## "c!"  auto  ANS core
0009E0r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CStore"""
0009E0r 3               xt_c_store:
0009E0r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
0009E3r 3               
0009E3r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
0009E5r 3  81 00                        sta (0,x)
0009E7r 3               
0009E7r 3  E8                           inx
0009E8r 3  E8                           inx
0009E9r 3  E8                           inx
0009EAr 3  E8                           inx
0009EBr 3               
0009EBr 3  60           z_c_store:      rts
0009ECr 3               
0009ECr 3               
0009ECr 3               ; ## CASE (C: -- 0) ( -- ) "Conditional flow control"
0009ECr 3               ; ## "case"  auto  ANS core ext
0009ECr 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CASE
0009ECr 3                       ;
0009ECr 3                       ; This is a dummy header, CASE shares the actual code with ZERO.
0009ECr 3                       ; """
0009ECr 3               
0009ECr 3               
0009ECr 3               ; ## CELL_PLUS ( u -- u ) "Add cell size in bytes"
0009ECr 3               ; ## "cell+"  auto  ANS core
0009ECr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CELLPlus
0009ECr 3                       ; Add the number of bytes ("address units") that one cell needs.
0009ECr 3                       ; Since this is an 8 bit machine with 16 bit cells, we add two bytes.
0009ECr 3                       ; """
0009ECr 3               
0009ECr 3               xt_cell_plus:
0009ECr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0009EFr 3               
0009EFr 3  F6 00                        inc 0,x
0009F1r 3  D0 02                        bne @1
0009F3r 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x
0009F5r 3               @1:
0009F5r 3  F6 00                        inc 0,x
0009F7r 3  D0 02                        bne @done
0009F9r 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x
0009FBr 3               @done:
0009FBr 3  60           z_cell_plus:    rts
0009FCr 3               
0009FCr 3               
0009FCr 3               
0009FCr 3               ; ## CELLS ( u -- u ) "Convert cells to size in bytes"
0009FCr 3               ; ## "cells"  auto  ANS core
0009FCr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CELLS
0009FCr 3                       ;
0009FCr 3                       ; Dummy entry for the CELLS word, the code is the same as for
0009FCr 3                       ; 2*, which is where the header directs us to
0009FCr 3                       ; """
0009FCr 3               
0009FCr 3               
0009FCr 3               ; ## CHAR ( "c" -- u ) "Convert character to ASCII value"
0009FCr 3               ; ## "char"  auto  ANS core
0009FCr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CHAR"""
0009FCr 3               
0009FCr 3               xt_char:
0009FCr 3                               ; get character from string, returns ( addr u )
0009FCr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_parse_name
0009FFr 3               
0009FFr 3                               ; if we got back a zero, we have a problem
0009FFr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000A01r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
000A03r 3  D0 05                        bne @not_empty
000A05r 3               
000A05r 3  A9 05                        lda #err_noname
000A07r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
000A0Ar 3               
000A0Ar 3               @not_empty:
000A0Ar 3  E8                           inx             ; drop number of characters, leave addr
000A0Br 3  E8                           inx
000A0Cr 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)       ; get character (equivalent to C@)
000A0Er 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
000A10r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; MSB is always zero
000A12r 3               
000A12r 3  60           z_char:         rts
000A13r 3               
000A13r 3               
000A13r 3               
000A13r 3               ; ## CHAR_PLUS ( addr -- addr+1 ) "Add the size of a character unit to address"
000A13r 3               ; ## "char+"  auto  ANS core
000A13r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CHARPlus
000A13r 3                       ;
000A13r 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the code is shared with ONE_PLUS
000A13r 3                       ; """
000A13r 3               
000A13r 3               
000A13r 3               ; ## CHARS ( n -- n ) "Number of bytes that n chars need"
000A13r 3               ; ## "chars"  auto  ANS core
000A13r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CHARS
000A13r 3                       ; Return how many address units n chars are. Since this is an 8 bit
000A13r 3                       ; machine, this does absolutely nothing and is included for
000A13r 3                       ; compatibility with other Forth versions
000A13r 3                       ; """
000A13r 3               
000A13r 3               xt_chars:
000A13r 3                               ; Checking for underflow seems a bit stupid because this
000A13r 3                               ; routine does nothing on this machine. However, the user
000A13r 3                               ; should be warned that there is something wrong with the
000A13r 3                               ; code if this occurs.
000A13r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
000A16r 3               
000A16r 3  60           z_chars:        rts
000A17r 3               
000A17r 3               
000A17r 3               ; ## CLEAVE ( addr u -- addr2 u2 addr1 u1 ) "Split off word from string"
000A17r 3               ; ## "cleave"  auto  Tali Forth
000A17r 3               
000A17r 3                       ; """Given a range of memory with words delimited by whitespace,return
000A17r 3                       ; the first word at the top of the stack and the rest of the word
000A17r 3                       ; following it.
000A17r 3                       ;
000A17r 3                       ; Example:
000A17r 3                       ; s" w1 w2 w3" cleave  -> "w2 w3" "w1"
000A17r 3                       ; s" w1" cleave        -> "" "w1"
000A17r 3                       ;
000A17r 3                       ; Since it will be used in loops a lot, we want it to work in pure
000A17r 3                       ; assembler and be as fast as we can make it. Calls PARSE-NAME so we
000A17r 3                       ; strip leading delimiters.
000A17r 3                       ; """
000A17r 3               
000A17r 3               xt_cleave:
000A17r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
000A1Ar 3               
000A1Ar 3                               ; We arrive here with ( addr u ). We need to strip any leading
000A1Ar 3                               ; spaces by hand: PARSE-NAME does do that, but it doesn't
000A1Ar 3                               ; remember how many spaces were stripped. This means we can't
000A1Ar 3                               ; calculate the length of the remainder. Fortunately, Tali
000A1Ar 3                               ; Forth has just the word we need for this:
000A1Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_minus_leading    ; -LEADING ( addr u )
000A1Dr 3               
000A1Dr 3                               ; The main part we can turn over to PARSE-NAME, except that we
000A1Dr 3                               ; have a string ( addr u ) and not stuff in the input buffer.
000A1Dr 3                               ; We get around this by cheating: We place ( addr u ) in the
000A1Dr 3                               ; input buffer and then call PARSE-NAME.
000A1Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_input_to_r       ; save old imput state
000A20r 3               
000A20r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x         ; u is new ciblen
000A22r 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen
000A24r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
000A26r 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen+1
000A28r 3               
000A28r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x         ; addr is new cib
000A2Ar 3  85 rr                        sta cib
000A2Cr 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
000A2Er 3  85 rr                        sta cib+1
000A30r 3               
000A30r 3  64 rr                        stz toin        ; >IN pointer is zero
000A32r 3  64 rr                        stz toin+1
000A34r 3               
000A34r 3                               ; PARSE-NAME gives us back the substring of the first word
000A34r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_parse_name       ; ( addr u addr-s u-s )
000A37r 3               
000A37r 3                               ; If we were given an empty string, then we're done. It's the
000A37r 3                               ; resposibility of the user to catch this as a sign to end the
000A37r 3                               ; any loop
000A37r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000A39r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
000A3Br 3  F0 23                        beq @done
000A3Dr 3               
000A3Dr 3                               ; Now we have to adjust the original string
000A3Dr 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x         ; LSB of original u
000A3Fr 3  38                           sec
000A40r 3  F5 00                        sbc 0,x
000A42r 3  95 04                        sta 4,x
000A44r 3               
000A44r 3  B5 05                        lda 5,x         ; MSB of original u
000A46r 3  F5 01                        sbc 1,x
000A48r 3  95 05                        sta 5,x
000A4Ar 3               
000A4Ar 3  B5 06                        lda 6,x         ; LSB of original addr
000A4Cr 3  18                           clc
000A4Dr 3  75 00                        adc 0,x
000A4Fr 3  95 06                        sta 6,x
000A51r 3               
000A51r 3  B5 07                        lda 7,x         ; MSB of original addr
000A53r 3  75 01                        adc 1,x
000A55r 3  95 07                        sta 7,x
000A57r 3               
000A57r 3                               ; There is one small problem: PARSE-NAME will probably have
000A57r 3                               ; left the string with the rest of the words with leading
000A57r 3                               ; delimiters. We use our magic -LEADING again
000A57r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_swap         ; ( addr-s u-s addr u )
000A5Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_minus_leading
000A5Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_swap         ; ( addr u addr-s u-s )
000A60r 3               @done:
000A60r 3                               ; Restore input
000A60r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_to_input
000A63r 3               
000A63r 3  60           z_cleave:       rts
000A64r 3               
000A64r 3               
000A64r 3               
000A64r 3               ; ## CMOVE ( addr1 addr2 u -- ) "Copy bytes going from low to high"
000A64r 3               ; ## "cmove"  auto  ANS string
000A64r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/string/CMOVE
000A64r 3                       ; Copy u bytes from addr1 to addr2, going low to high (addr2 is
000A64r 3                       ; larger than addr1). Based on code in Leventhal, Lance A.
000A64r 3                       ; "6502 Assembly Language Routines", p. 201, where it is called
000A64r 3                       ; "move left".
000A64r 3                       ;
000A64r 3                       ; There are no official tests for this word.
000A64r 3                       ; """
000A64r 3               
000A64r 3               xt_cmove:
000A64r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
000A67r 3               
000A67r 3                               ; move destination address to where we can work with it
000A67r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
000A69r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2        ; use tmp2 because easier to remember
000A6Br 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
000A6Dr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
000A6Fr 3               
000A6Fr 3                               ; move source address to where we can work with it
000A6Fr 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x
000A71r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1        ; use tmp1 because easier to remember
000A73r 3  B5 05                        lda 5,x
000A75r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
000A77r 3               
000A77r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0
000A79r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x         ; number of whole pages to move
000A7Br 3  F0 0F                        beq @dopartial
000A7Dr 3               
000A7Dr 3               @page:
000A7Dr 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
000A7Fr 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp2),y
000A81r 3  C8                           iny
000A82r 3  D0 F9                        bne @page
000A84r 3               
000A84r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1+1
000A86r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2+1
000A88r 3  D6 01                        dec 1,x
000A8Ar 3  D0 F1                        bne @page
000A8Cr 3               
000A8Cr 3               @dopartial:
000A8Cr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x         ; length of last page
000A8Er 3  F0 09                        beq @done
000A90r 3               
000A90r 3               @partial:
000A90r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
000A92r 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp2),y
000A94r 3  C8                           iny
000A95r 3               
000A95r 3  D6 00                        dec 0,x
000A97r 3  D0 F7                        bne @partial
000A99r 3               
000A99r 3               @done:          ; clear the stack
000A99r 3  8A                           txa
000A9Ar 3  18                           clc
000A9Br 3  69 06                        adc #6
000A9Dr 3  AA                           tax
000A9Er 3               
000A9Er 3  60           z_cmove:        rts
000A9Fr 3               
000A9Fr 3               
000A9Fr 3               
000A9Fr 3               ; ## CMOVE_UP ( add1 add2 u -- ) "Copy bytes from high to low"
000A9Fr 3               ; ## "cmove>"  auto  ANS string
000A9Fr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/string/CMOVEtop
000A9Fr 3                       ; Based on code in Leventhal, Lance A. "6502 Assembly Language
000A9Fr 3                       ; Routines", p. 201, where it is called "move right".
000A9Fr 3                       ;
000A9Fr 3                       ; There are no official tests for this word.
000A9Fr 3                       ; """
000A9Fr 3               
000A9Fr 3               xt_cmove_up:
000A9Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
000AA2r 3               
000AA2r 3                               ; Move destination address to where we can work with it
000AA2r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
000AA4r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2        ; use tmp2 because easier to remember
000AA6r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
000AA8r 3  18                           clc
000AA9r 3  75 01                        adc 1,x
000AABr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1      ; point to last page of destination
000AADr 3               
000AADr 3                               ; Move source address to where we can work with it
000AADr 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x
000AAFr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1        ; use tmp1 because easier to remember
000AB1r 3  B5 05                        lda 5,x
000AB3r 3  18                           clc
000AB4r 3  75 01                        adc 1,x
000AB6r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1      ; point to last page of source
000AB8r 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x         ; allows us to use bne with dec 1,x below
000ABAr 3               
000ABAr 3                               ; Move the last partial page first
000ABAr 3  B4 00                        ldy 0,x         ; length of last page
000ABCr 3  F0 0E                        beq @nopartial
000ABEr 3               
000ABEr 3               @outerloop:
000ABEr 3  88                           dey
000ABFr 3  F0 07                        beq @finishpage
000AC1r 3               
000AC1r 3               @innerloop:
000AC1r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
000AC3r 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp2),y
000AC5r 3  88                           dey
000AC6r 3  D0 F9                        bne @innerloop
000AC8r 3               
000AC8r 3               @finishpage:
000AC8r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)      ; handle y = 0 separately
000ACAr 3  92 rr                        sta (tmp2)
000ACCr 3               
000ACCr 3               @nopartial:
000ACCr 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp1+1      ; back up to previous pages
000ACEr 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp2+1
000AD0r 3  D6 01                        dec 1,x
000AD2r 3  D0 EA                        bne @outerloop
000AD4r 3               @done:
000AD4r 3                               ; clear up the stack and leave
000AD4r 3  8A                           txa
000AD5r 3  18                           clc
000AD6r 3  69 06                        adc #6
000AD8r 3  AA                           tax
000AD9r 3               
000AD9r 3  60           z_cmove_up:     rts
000ADAr 3               
000ADAr 3               
000ADAr 3               
000ADAr 3               ; ## COLON ( "name" -- ) "Start compilation of a new word"
000ADAr 3               ; ## ":"  auto  ANS core
000ADAr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Colon
000ADAr 3                       ;
000ADAr 3                       ; Use the CREATE routine and fill in the rest by hand.
000ADAr 3                       ; """
000ADAr 3               
000ADAr 3               xt_colon:
000ADAr 3                               ; If we're already in the compile state, complain
000ADAr 3                               ; and quit
000ADAr 3  A5 rr                        lda state
000ADCr 3  05 rr                        ora state+1
000ADEr 3  F0 05                        beq @1
000AE0r 3               
000AE0r 3  A9 07                        lda #err_state
000AE2r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
000AE5r 3               @1:
000AE5r 3                               ; switch to compile state
000AE5r 3  C6 rr                        dec state
000AE7r 3  C6 rr                        dec state+1
000AE9r 3               
000AE9r 3                               ; Set bit 6 in status to tell ";" and RECURSE this is a normal
000AE9r 3                               ; word
000AE9r 3  A9 40                        lda #%01000000
000AEBr 3  04 rr                        tsb status
000AEDr 3               
000AEDr 3                               ; CREATE is going to change the DP to point to the new word's
000AEDr 3                               ; header. While this is fine for (say) variables, it would mean
000AEDr 3                               ; that FIND-NAME etc would find a half-finished word when
000AEDr 3                               ; looking in the Dictionary. To prevent this, we save the old
000AEDr 3                               ; version of DP and restore it later. The new DP is placed in
000AEDr 3                               ; the variable WORKWORD until we're finished with a SEMICOLON.
000AEDr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr current_to_dp
000AF0r 3  A5 rr                        lda dp+1            ; CREATE uses a lot of variables
000AF2r 3  48                           pha
000AF3r 3  A5 rr                        lda dp
000AF5r 3  48                           pha
000AF6r 3               
000AF6r 3                               ; Tell create not to print warning for duplicate name.
000AF6r 3  A9 80                        lda #%10000000
000AF8r 3  04 rr                        tsb status
000AFAr 3               
000AFAr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_create
000AFDr 3               
000AFDr 3                               ; Get the nt (not the xt!) of the new word as described above.
000AFDr 3                               ; Only COLON, SEMICOLON and RECURSE get to access WORKWORD
000AFDr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr current_to_dp   ; This might be able to be omitted
000B00r 3  A5 rr                        lda dp
000B02r 3  85 rr                        sta workword
000B04r 3  A5 rr                        lda dp+1
000B06r 3  85 rr                        sta workword+1
000B08r 3               
000B08r 3                               ; Restore original DP
000B08r 3  68                           pla
000B09r 3  85 rr                        sta dp
000B0Br 3  68                           pla
000B0Cr 3  85 rr                        sta dp+1
000B0Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr dp_to_current
000B11r 3               
000B11r 3                               ; CREATE includes a subroutine jump to DOVAR by default. We
000B11r 3                               ; back up three bytes and overwrite that.
000B11r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
000B13r 3  38                           sec
000B14r 3  E9 03                        sbc #3
000B16r 3  85 rr                        sta cp
000B18r 3  B0 02                        bcs @done
000B1Ar 3  C6 rr                        dec cp+1
000B1Cr 3               @done:
000B1Cr 3  60           z_colon:        rts
000B1Dr 3               
000B1Dr 3               
000B1Dr 3               ; ## COLON_NONAME ( -- ) "Start compilation of a new word""
000B1Dr 3               ; ## ":NONAME"  auto  ANS core
000B1Dr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ColonNONAME
000B1Dr 3                       ; Compile a word with no nt.  ";" will put its xt on the stack.
000B1Dr 3                       ; """
000B1Dr 3               
000B1Dr 3               xt_colon_noname:
000B1Dr 3                               ; If we're already in the compile state, complain
000B1Dr 3                               ; and quit
000B1Dr 3  A5 rr                        lda state
000B1Fr 3  05 rr                        ora state+1
000B21r 3  F0 05                        beq @1
000B23r 3               
000B23r 3  A9 07                        lda #err_state
000B25r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
000B28r 3               @1:
000B28r 3                               ; switch to compile state
000B28r 3  C6 rr                        dec state
000B2Ar 3  C6 rr                        dec state+1
000B2Cr 3               
000B2Cr 3                               ; Clear bit 6 in status to tell ";" and RECURSE this is
000B2Cr 3                               ; a :NONAME word.
000B2Cr 3  A9 40                        lda #%01000000
000B2Er 3  14 rr                        trb status
000B30r 3               
000B30r 3                               ; Put cp (the xt for this word) in WORKWORD. The flag above
000B30r 3                               ; lets both ";" and RECURSE know that is is an xt instead of an
000B30r 3                               ; nt and they will modify their behavior.
000B30r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
000B32r 3  85 rr                        sta workword
000B34r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
000B36r 3  85 rr                        sta workword+1
000B38r 3               @done:
000B38r 3  60           z_colon_noname:        rts
000B39r 3               
000B39r 3               
000B39r 3               
000B39r 3               ; ## COMMA ( n -- ) "Allot and store one cell in memory"
000B39r 3               ; ## ","  auto  ANS core
000B39r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Comma
000B39r 3                       ; Store TOS at current place in memory.
000B39r 3                       ;
000B39r 3                       ; Since this an eight-bit machine, we can ignore all alignment issues.
000B39r 3                       ; """
000B39r 3               
000B39r 3               xt_comma:
000B39r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
000B3Cr 3               
000B3Cr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000B3Er 3  92 rr                        sta (cp)
000B40r 3               
000B40r 3  E6 rr                        inc cp
000B42r 3  D0 02                        bne @1
000B44r 3  E6 rr                        inc cp+1
000B46r 3               @1:
000B46r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
000B48r 3  92 rr                        sta (cp)
000B4Ar 3               
000B4Ar 3  E6 rr                        inc cp
000B4Cr 3  D0 02                        bne @done
000B4Er 3  E6 rr                        inc cp+1
000B50r 3               @done:
000B50r 3  E8                           inx
000B51r 3  E8                           inx
000B52r 3               
000B52r 3  60           z_comma:        rts
000B53r 3               
000B53r 3               
000B53r 3               
000B53r 3               ; ## COMPARE ( addr1 u1 addr2 u2 -- -1 | 0 | 1) "Compare two strings"
000B53r 3               ; ## "compare"   auto  ANS string
000B53r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/string/COMPARE
000B53r 3                       ; Compare string1 (denoted by addr1 u1) to string2 (denoted by
000B53r 3                       ; addr2 u2).  Return -1 if string1 < string2, 0 if string1 = string2
000B53r 3                       ; and 1 if string1 > string2 (ASCIIbetical comparison).  A string
000B53r 3                       ; that entirely matches the beginning of the other string, but is
000B53r 3                       ; shorter, is considered less than the longer string.
000B53r 3                       ; """
000B53r 3               
000B53r 3               xt_compare:
000B53r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_4
000B56r 3               
000B56r 3                               ; Load the two string addresses into tmp1 and tmp2.
000B56r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
000B58r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
000B5Ar 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
000B5Cr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
000B5Er 3  B5 06                        lda 6,x
000B60r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
000B62r 3  B5 07                        lda 7,x
000B64r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
000B66r 3                               ; The counts will be used in-place on the stack.
000B66r 3               
000B66r 3               @compare_loop:
000B66r 3                               ; Check to see if we are out of letters.
000B66r 3               
000B66r 3                               ; Check string1
000B66r 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x
000B68r 3  15 05                        ora 5,x
000B6Ar 3  F0 2C                        beq @str1_done
000B6Cr 3               
000B6Cr 3                               ; Check string2
000B6Cr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000B6Er 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
000B70r 3  F0 3A                        beq @greater    ; Str2 empty first
000B72r 3               
000B72r 3               @check_letter:
000B72r 3                               ; Both strings have at least one letter left.
000B72r 3                               ; Check the letters against each other.
000B72r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)
000B74r 3  D2 rr                        cmp (tmp2)
000B76r 3  90 26                        bcc @less
000B78r 3  D0 32                        bne @greater
000B7Ar 3               @next_letter:
000B7Ar 3                               ; Move both tmp pointers and decrement the counts
000B7Ar 3                               ; on the stack.
000B7Ar 3                               ; Increment tmp1
000B7Ar 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1
000B7Cr 3  D0 02                        bne @1
000B7Er 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1+1
000B80r 3               @1:
000B80r 3                               ; Increment tmp2
000B80r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2
000B82r 3  D0 02                        bne @2
000B84r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2+1
000B86r 3               @2:
000B86r 3                               ; Decrement count1 on the stack.
000B86r 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x
000B88r 3  D0 02                        bne @3
000B8Ar 3  D6 05                        dec 5,x
000B8Cr 3               @3:
000B8Cr 3  D6 04                        dec 4,x
000B8Er 3               
000B8Er 3                               ; Decrement count2 on the stack.
000B8Er 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000B90r 3  D0 02                        bne @4
000B92r 3  D6 01                        dec 1,x
000B94r 3               @4:
000B94r 3  D6 00                        dec 0,x
000B96r 3               
000B96r 3                               ; Loop around and check again.
000B96r 3  80 CE                        bra @compare_loop
000B98r 3               
000B98r 3               @str1_done:
000B98r 3                               ; String 1 is out of letters. Check string 2.
000B98r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000B9Ar 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
000B9Cr 3  F0 08                        beq @equal      ; Both out of letters
000B9Er 3               
000B9Er 3                               ; Falls into less (str1 is out but str2 has more)
000B9Er 3               @less:
000B9Er 3                               ; Return -1
000B9Er 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF
000BA0r 3  95 06                        sta 6,x
000BA2r 3  95 07                        sta 7,x
