0010FCr 3               
0010FCr 3               
0010FCr 3               ; ## DUMP ( addr u -- ) "Display a memory region"
0010FCr 3               ; ## "dump"  tested  ANS tools
0010FCr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/tools/DUMP
0010FCr 3                       ;
0010FCr 3                       ; DUMP's exact output is defined as "implementation dependent".
0010FCr 3                       ; This is in assembler because it is
0010FCr 3                       ; useful for testing and development, so we want to have it work
0010FCr 3                       ; as soon as possible. Uses TMP2
0010FCr 3                       ; """
0010FCr 3               
0010FCr 3               xt_dump:
0010FCr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
0010FFr 3               @row:
0010FFr 3                               ; start counter for 16 numbers per row
0010FFr 3  A0 10                        ldy #16
001101r 3               
001101r 3                               ; We use TMP2 as the index for the ASCII characters
001101r 3                               ; that we print at the and of the hex block. We
001101r 3                               ; start saving them at HERE (CP)
001101r 3  64 rr                        stz tmp2
001103r 3               
001103r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_cr
001106r 3               
001106r 3                               ; print address number
001106r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
001108r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr byte_to_ascii
00110Br 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
00110Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr byte_to_ascii
001110r 3               
001110r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
001113r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
001116r 3               @loop:
001116r 3                               ; if there are zero bytes left to display, we're done
001116r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001118r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
00111Ar 3  F0 39                        beq @all_printed
00111Cr 3               
00111Cr 3                               ; dump the contents
00111Cr 3  A1 02                        lda (2,x)
00111Er 3  48                           pha                     ; byte_to_ascii destroys A
00111Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr byte_to_ascii
001122r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
001125r 3  68                           pla
001126r 3               
001126r 3                               ; Handle ASCII printing
001126r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr is_printable
001129r 3  B0 02                        bcs @printable
00112Br 3  A9 2E                        lda #'.'                 ; Print dot if not printable
00112Dr 3               @printable:
00112Dr 3  5A                           phy                     ; save counter
00112Er 3  A4 rr                        ldy tmp2
001130r 3  91 rr                        sta (cp),y
001132r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2
001134r 3  7A                           ply
001135r 3               
001135r 3                               ; extra space after eight bytes
001135r 3  C0 09                        cpy #9
001137r 3  D0 03                        bne @next_char
001139r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
00113Cr 3               
00113Cr 3               @next_char:
00113Cr 3  F6 02                        inc 2,x
00113Er 3  D0 02                        bne @counter
001140r 3  F6 03                        inc 3,x
001142r 3               
001142r 3               @counter:
001142r 3                               ; loop counter
001142r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001144r 3  D0 02                        bne @1
001146r 3  D6 01                        dec 1,x
001148r 3               @1:
001148r 3  D6 00                        dec 0,x
00114Ar 3  88                           dey
00114Br 3  D0 C9                        bne @loop               ; next byte
00114Dr 3               
00114Dr 3                               ; Done with one line, print the ASCII version of these
00114Dr 3                               ; characters
00114Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
001150r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_ascii
001153r 3               
001153r 3  80 AA                        bra @row                ; new row
001155r 3               
001155r 3               @all_printed:
001155r 3                               ; See if there are any ASCII characters in the buffer
001155r 3                               ; left to print
001155r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2
001157r 3  F0 06                        beq @done
001159r 3               
001159r 3                               ; In theory, we could try to make the ASCII part line
001159r 3                               ; up with the line before it. But that is a hassle (we
001159r 3                               ; use three bytes for each missed hex entry, and
001159r 3                               ; then there is the gap after eight entries) and it
001159r 3                               ; makes it harder to read. We settle for one extra
001159r 3                               ; space instead for the moment
001159r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
00115Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_ascii
00115Fr 3               @done:
00115Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_drop         ; one byte less than 4x INX
001162r 3  60           z_dump:         rts
001163r 3               
001163r 3               
001163r 3               print_ascii:
001163r 3                               ; Print the ASCII characters that we have saved from
001163r 3                               ; HERE (CP) to HERE plus whatever is in TMP2. This routine
001163r 3                               ; is not compiled (DUMP is probably never compiled anyway)
001163r 3                               ; but we keep it inside the scope of DUMP.
001163r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0
001165r 3               @ascii_loop:
001165r 3  B1 rr                        lda (cp),y
001167r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
00116Ar 3  C8                           iny
00116Br 3               
00116Br 3                               ; extra space after eight chars
00116Br 3  C0 08                        cpy #8
00116Dr 3  D0 03                        bne @1
00116Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
001172r 3               @1:
001172r 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp2
001174r 3  D0 EF                        bne @ascii_loop
001176r 3               
001176r 3  60                           rts
001177r 3               
001177r 3               
001177r 3               
001177r 3               ; ## DUP ( u -- u u ) "Duplicate TOS"
001177r 3               ; ## "dup"  auto  ANS core
001177r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/DUP"""
001177r 3               xt_dup:
001177r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
00117Ar 3               
00117Ar 3  CA                           dex
00117Br 3  CA                           dex
00117Cr 3               
00117Cr 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x         ; LSB
00117Er 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001180r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x         ; MSB
001182r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001184r 3               
001184r 3  60           z_dup:          rts
001185r 3               
001185r 3               
001185r 3               ; ## ED ( -- u ) "Line-based editor"
001185r 3               ; ## "ed"  fragment  Tali Forth
001185r 3                       ; """Start the line-based editor ed6502. See separate file
001185r 3                       ; ed.asm or the manual for details.
001185r 3                       ; """
001185r 3               xt_ed:
001185r 3                           .ifdef ed6502
001185r 3                               jsr ed6502      ; kept in separate file
001185r 3                           .endif
001185r 3               
001185r 3  60           z_ed:           rts
001186r 3               
001186r 3               
001186r 3               ; ## EDITOR_WORDLIST ( -- u ) "WID for the Editor wordlist"
001186r 3               ; ## "editor-wordlist"  tested  Tali Editor
001186r 3                       ; """ Commonly used like `editor-wordlist >order` to add the editor
001186r 3                       ; words to the search order so they can be used.  This will need
001186r 3                       ; to be done before any of the words marked "Tali Editor" can be
001186r 3                       ; used.  See the tutorial on Wordlists and the Search Order for
001186r 3                       ; more information.
001186r 3               
001186r 3                       ;
001186r 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the code is shared with ONE
001186r 3                       ; """
001186r 3               
001186r 3               
001186r 3               ; ## ELSE (C: orig -- orig) ( -- ) "Conditional flow control"
001186r 3               ; ## "else"  auto  ANS core
001186r 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ELSE
001186r 3                       ;
001186r 3                       ; The code is shared with ENDOF
001186r 3                       ; """
001186r 3               
001186r 3               xt_else:
001186r 3               xt_endof:
001186r 3                               ; Put an unconditional branch.
001186r 3  A0 rr                        ldy #>branch_runtime
001188r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<branch_runtime
00118Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_subroutine
00118Dr 3               
00118Dr 3                               ; Put the address of the branch address on the stack.
00118Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_here
001190r 3               
001190r 3                               ; Use zero for the branch address for now.
001190r 3                               ; THEN will fill it in later.
001190r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_zero
001193r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_comma
001196r 3               
001196r 3                               ; Get the address to jump to (just after the
001196r 3                               ; unconditional branch) for the IF to jump to
001196r 3                               ; when false.
001196r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_here
001199r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_rot
00119Cr 3               
00119Cr 3                               ; Update the original if 0branch address.
00119Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_store
00119Fr 3               z_else:
00119Fr 3               z_endof:
00119Fr 3  60                           rts
0011A0r 3               
0011A0r 3               
0011A0r 3               
0011A0r 3               branch_runtime:
0011A0r 3                       ; """Runtime component for a branch. Used by ELSE and ENDOF. This was
0011A0r 3                       ; formally part of a separate word BRANCH which was later removed.
0011A0r 3                       ; """
0011A0r 3               
0011A0r 3                               ; The address on the Return Stack points to the last byte
0011A0r 3                               ; of the JSR address, one byte below the branch literal
0011A0r 3  68                           pla
0011A1r 3  85 rr                        sta tmpbranch
0011A3r 3  68                           pla
0011A4r 3  85 rr                        sta tmpbranch+1
0011A6r 3               
0011A6r 3                               ; Keep in mind: the address we just popped points one byte
0011A6r 3                               ; lower than the branch literal we want to grab
0011A6r 3  A0 01                        ldy #1
0011A8r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmpbranch),y  ; LSB
0011AAr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
0011ACr 3  C8                           iny
0011ADr 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmpbranch),y  ; MSB
0011AFr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
0011B1r 3               
0011B1r 3  6C rr rr                     jmp (tmp1)
0011B4r 3               
0011B4r 3               
0011B4r 3               
0011B4r 3               ; ## EMIT ( char -- ) "Print character to current output"
0011B4r 3               ; ## "emit"  auto  ANS core
0011B4r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/EMIT
0011B4r 3                       ; Run-time default for EMIT. The user can revector this by changing
0011B4r 3                       ; the value of the OUTPUT variable. We ignore the MSB completely, and
0011B4r 3                       ; do not check to see if we have been given a valid ASCII character.
0011B4r 3                       ; Don't make this native compile.
0011B4r 3                       ; """
0011B4r 3               
0011B4r 3               xt_emit:
0011B4r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0011B7r 3               
0011B7r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0011B9r 3  E8                           inx
0011BAr 3  E8                           inx
0011BBr 3               
0011BBr 3               emit_a:
0011BBr 3                       ; We frequently want to print the character in A without fooling
0011BBr 3                       ; around with the Data Stack. This is emit_a's job, which still
0011BBr 3                       ; allows the output to be vectored. Call it with JSR as you
0011BBr 3                       ; would XT_EMIT
0011BBr 3  6C rr rr                     jmp (output)            ; JSR/RTS
0011BEr 3               
0011BEr 3               z_emit:         ; never reached
0011BEr 3               
0011BEr 3               
0011BEr 3               
0011BEr 3               ; ## EMPTY_BUFFERS ( -- ) "Empty all buffers without saving"
0011BEr 3               ; ## "empty-buffers"  tested  ANS block ext
0011BEr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/EMPTY-BUFFERS"""
0011BEr 3               xt_empty_buffers:
0011BEr 3                               ; Set the buffer status to empty.
0011BEr 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
0011C0r 3  A9 00                        lda #0
0011C2r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y      ; Only LSB is used.
0011C4r 3               z_empty_buffers:
0011C4r 3  60                           rts
0011C5r 3               
0011C5r 3               
0011C5r 3               ; ## ENDCASE (C: case-sys -- ) ( x -- ) "Conditional flow control"
0011C5r 3               ; ## "endcase"  auto  ANS core ext
0011C5r 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ENDCASE"""
0011C5r 3               
0011C5r 3               xt_endcase:
0011C5r 3                               ; Postpone DROP to remove the item
0011C5r 3                               ; being checked.
0011C5r 3  A0 rr                        ldy #>xt_drop
0011C7r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<xt_drop
0011C9r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_subroutine
0011CCr 3               
0011CCr 3                               ; There are a number of address (of branches that need their
0011CCr 3                               ; jump addressed filled in with the address of right here).
0011CCr 3                               ; Keep calling THEN to deal with them until we reach the
0011CCr 3                               ; 0 that CASE put on the stack at the beginning.
0011CCr 3               @endcase_loop:
0011CCr 3                               ; Check for 0 on the stack.
0011CCr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0011CEr 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
0011D0r 3  F0 05                        beq @done
0011D2r 3               
0011D2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_then
0011D5r 3  80 F5                        bra @endcase_loop
0011D7r 3               @done:
0011D7r 3                               ; Remove the 0 from the stack.
0011D7r 3  E8                           inx
0011D8r 3  E8                           inx
0011D9r 3  60           z_endcase:      rts
0011DAr 3               
0011DAr 3               
0011DAr 3               
0011DAr 3               ; ## ENDOF (C: case-sys1 of-sys1-- case-sys2) ( -- ) "Conditional flow control"
0011DAr 3               ; ## "endof"  auto  ANS core ext
0011DAr 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ENDOF
0011DAr 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the code is shared with ELSE
0011DAr 3                       ; """
0011DAr 3               
0011DAr 3               
0011DAr 3               ; ## ENVIRONMENT_Q  ( addr u -- 0 | i*x true )  "Return system information"
0011DAr 3               ; ## "environment?"  auto  ANS core
0011DAr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ENVIRONMENTq
0011DAr 3                       ;
0011DAr 3                       ; By ANS definition, we use upper-case strings here, see the
0011DAr 3                       ; string file for details. This can be realized as a high-level
0011DAr 3                       ; Forth word as
0011DAr 3                       ;
0011DAr 3                       ; : STRING_OF POSTPONE 2OVER POSTPONE COMPARE POSTPONE 0=
0011DAr 3                       ;    POSTPONE IF POSTPONE 2DROP ; IMMEDIATE COMPILE-ONLY
0011DAr 3                       ; HEX
0011DAr 3                       ; : ENVIRONMENT? ( C-ADDR U -- FALSE | I*X TRUE )
0011DAr 3                       ; CASE
0011DAr 3                       ; S" /COUNTED-STRING"    STRING_OF  7FFF TRUE ENDOF
0011DAr 3                       ; S" /HOLD"              STRING_OF    FF TRUE ENDOF
0011DAr 3                       ; S" /PAD"               STRING_OF    54 TRUE ENDOF ( 84 DECIMAL )
0011DAr 3                       ; S" ADDRESS-UNIT-BITS"  STRING_OF     8 TRUE ENDOF
0011DAr 3                       ; S" FLOORED"            STRING_OF FALSE TRUE ENDOF ( WE HAVE SYMMETRIC )
0011DAr 3                       ; S" MAX-CHAR"           STRING_OF   255 TRUE ENDOF
0011DAr 3                       ; S" MAX-D"              STRING_OF
0011DAr 3                                                    ; 7FFFFFFF. TRUE ENDOF
0011DAr 3                       ; S" MAX-N"              STRING_OF  7FFF TRUE ENDOF
0011DAr 3                       ; S" MAX-U"              STRING_OF  FFFF TRUE ENDOF
0011DAr 3                       ; S" MAX-UD"             STRING_OF
0011DAr 3                                                    ; FFFFFFFF. TRUE ENDOF
0011DAr 3                       ; S" RETURN-STACK-CELLS" STRING_OF    80 TRUE ENDOF
0011DAr 3                       ; S" STACK-CELLS"        STRING_OF    20 TRUE ENDOF ( FROM DEFINITIONS.ASM )
0011DAr 3                       ; ( DEFAULT ) 2DROP FALSE FALSE ( ONE FALSE WILL DROPPED BY ENDCASE )
0011DAr 3                       ; ENDCASE ;
0011DAr 3                       ;
0011DAr 3                       ; but that uses lots of memory and increases the start up time. This
0011DAr 3                       ; word is rarely used so we can try to keep it short at the expense
0011DAr 3                       ; of speed.
0011DAr 3                       ; """
0011DAr 3               
0011DAr 3               xt_environment_q:
0011DAr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0011DDr 3               
0011DDr 3                               ; This code is table-driven: We walk through the list of
0011DDr 3                               ; strings until we find one that matches, and then we take
0011DDr 3                               ; the equivalent data from the results table. This is made
0011DDr 3                               ; a bit harder by the fact that some of these return a
0011DDr 3                               ; double-cell number and some a single-cell one.
0011DDr 3               
0011DDr 3                               ; We will walk through the table with variables that return
0011DDr 3                               ; a single-cell result
0011DDr 3  A0 00                        ldy #00                 ; counter for table
0011DFr 3               
0011DFr 3                               ; We use a flag on the the stack to signal if we have a single-cell
0011DFr 3                               ; or double-cell number. We use 0 to signal single-cell and 1 for
0011DFr 3                               ; double-cell.
0011DFr 3  5A                           phy
0011E0r 3               @table_loop:
0011E0r 3                               ; We arrived here with the address of the string to be checked
0011E0r 3                               ; on the stack. We make a copy. Index is in Y
0011E0r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_dup          ; ( addr u addr u ) 2DUP does not use Y
0011E3r 3               
0011E3r 3                               ; We do our work on the TOS to speed things up
0011E3r 3  CA                           dex
0011E4r 3  CA                           dex                     ; ( addr u addr u ? )
0011E5r 3               
0011E5r 3                               ; Get address of string to check from table
0011E5r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_table_single,y
0011E8r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0011EAr 3  C8                           iny
0011EBr 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_table_single,y
0011EEr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x                 ; ( addr u addr u addr-t )
0011F0r 3  C8                           iny
0011F1r 3               
0011F1r 3                               ; See if this is the last entry. The LSB is still in A
0011F1r 3  15 00                        ora 0,x
0011F3r 3  F0 4D                        beq @table_done
0011F5r 3               
0011F5r 3                               ; We have a string entry. The address there is stored in
0011F5r 3                               ; old-style address format, that is, the first byte is the
0011F5r 3                               ; length of the string
0011F5r 3  5A                           phy                     ; save Y, which is used by COUNT
0011F6r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_count            ; ( addr u addr u addr-s u-s )
0011F9r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_compare          ; ( addr u f )
0011FCr 3  7A                           ply
0011FDr 3               
0011FDr 3                               ; If we found a match (flag is zero -- COMPARE is weird
0011FDr 3                               ; that way), return the result
0011FDr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0011FFr 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
001201r 3  F0 04                        beq @got_result
001203r 3               
001203r 3                               ; Flag is not zero, so not a perfect match, so try next
001203r 3                               ; word
001203r 3  E8                           inx                     ; DROP, now ( addr u )
001204r 3  E8                           inx
001205r 3               
001205r 3  80 D9                        bra @table_loop
001207r 3               
001207r 3               @got_result:
001207r 3                               ; We arrive here with ( addr u -1 ) and know that we've found
001207r 3                               ; a match. The index of the match+2 is in Y.
001207r 3  E8                           inx                     ; drop flag, now ( addr u )
001208r 3  E8                           inx
001209r 3  88                           dey                     ; go back to index we had
00120Ar 3  88                           dey
00120Br 3               
00120Br 3                               ; See if this is a single-cell word.
00120Br 3  68                           pla
00120Cr 3  D0 0D                        bne @double_result
00120Er 3               
00120Er 3                               ; Single-cell result
00120Er 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_single,y
001211r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001213r 3  C8                           iny
001214r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_single,y
001217r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x                 ; ( res u )
001219r 3               
001219r 3  80 1F                        bra @set_flag
00121Br 3               
00121Br 3               @double_result:
00121Br 3                               ; This is a double-celled result, which means we have to
00121Br 3                               ; fool around with the index some more. We also need a
00121Br 3                               ; further cell on the stack
00121Br 3  CA                           dex                     ; ( addr u ? )
00121Cr 3  CA                           dex
00121Dr 3               
00121Dr 3                               ; We have 11 single-cell words we check, plus the 0000 as
00121Dr 3                               ; a marker for the end of the table, so we arrive here
00121Dr 3                               ; with Y as 22 or more. To get the index for the double-
00121Dr 3                               ; cell words, we move the result
00121Dr 3  98                           tya
00121Er 3  38                           sec
00121Fr 3  E9 18                        sbc #24
001221r 3               
001221r 3                               ; We have four bytes per entry in the table, but the index
001221r 3                               ; keeps increasing by two, so we only have to multiply by
001221r 3                               ; two (shift left once) to get the right result
001221r 3  0A                           asl
001222r 3  A8                           tay
001223r 3               
001223r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_double,y
001226r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001228r 3  C8                           iny
001229r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_double,y
00122Cr 3  95 03                        sta 3,x                 ; ( res u ? )
00122Er 3  C8                           iny
00122Fr 3               
00122Fr 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_double,y
001232r 3  95 04                        sta 4,x
001234r 3  C8                           iny
001235r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_double,y
001238r 3  95 05                        sta 5,x                 ; ( res res ? )
00123Ar 3               
00123Ar 3                               ; fall through to @set_flag
00123Ar 3               @set_flag:
00123Ar 3  A9 FF                        lda #$ff
00123Cr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00123Er 3  95 01                        sta 1,x                 ; ( res f )
001240r 3               
001240r 3  80 14                        bra @done
001242r 3               @table_done:
001242r 3                               ; We're done with a table, because the entry was a zero.
001242r 3                               ; We arrive here with ( addr u addr u 0 )
001242r 3               
001242r 3                               ; We take the flag from stack and increase it by one. If the
001242r 3                               ; flag is zero, we have just completed the single-cell number
001242r 3                               ; strings, so we in increase the flag and try again. Otherwise,
001242r 3                               ; we're done with the double-cell table without having found
001242r 3                               ; a match, and we're done
001242r 3  68                           pla
001243r 3  D0 09                        bne @no_match
001245r 3               
001245r 3                               ; Flag is zero, increase it to one and start over to check
001245r 3                               ; double-cell values
001245r 3  1A                           inc
001246r 3  48                           pha
001247r 3               
001247r 3  8A                           txa
001248r 3  18                           clc
001249r 3  69 06                        adc #6                  ; skip six bytes
00124Br 3  AA                           tax                     ; ( addr u )
00124Cr 3               
00124Cr 3  80 92                        bra @table_loop
00124Er 3               @no_match:
00124Er 3                               ; Bummer, not found. We arrive here with
00124Er 3                               ; ( addr u addr u 0 ) and need to return just a zero
00124Er 3  8A                           txa
00124Fr 3  18                           clc
001250r 3  69 0A                        adc #10
001252r 3  AA                           tax                     ; ( addr ) - not ( 0 ) !
001253r 3               
001253r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_false
001256r 3               @done:
001256r 3               z_environment_q:
001256r 3  60                           rts
001257r 3               
001257r 3               
001257r 3               ; Tables for ENVIRONMENT?. We use two separate ones, one for the single-cell
001257r 3               ; results and one for the double-celled results. The zero cell at the
001257r 3               ; end of each table marks its, uh, end. The strings themselves are defined
001257r 3               ; in strings.asm. Note if we add more entries to the single-cell table, we
001257r 3               ; have to adapt the result code for double printout, where we subtract 22
001257r 3               ; (two bytes each single-cell string and two bytes for the end-of-table
001257r 3               ; marker 0000
001257r 3               env_table_single:
001257r 3  rr rr rr rr          .word envs_cs, envs_hold, envs_pad, envs_aub, envs_floored
00125Br 3  rr rr rr rr  
00125Fr 3  rr rr        
001261r 3  rr rr rr rr          .word envs_max_char, envs_max_n, envs_max_u, envs_rsc
001265r 3  rr rr rr rr  
001269r 3  rr rr rr rr          .word envs_sc, envs_wl, 0000
00126Dr 3  00 00        
00126Fr 3               
00126Fr 3               env_table_double:
00126Fr 3  rr rr rr rr          .word envs_max_d, envs_max_ud, 0000
001273r 3  00 00        
001275r 3               
001275r 3               env_results_single:
001275r 3  FF 7F                .word $7FFF     ; /COUNTED-STRING
001277r 3  FF 00                .word $00FF     ; /HOLD
001279r 3  54 00                .word $0054     ; /PAD (this is 84 decimal)
00127Br 3  08 00                .word $0008     ; ADDRESS-UNIT-BITS (keep "$" to avoid octal!)
00127Dr 3  00 00                .word 0000      ; FLOORED ("FALSE", we have symmetric)
00127Fr 3  FF 00                .word $00FF     ; MAX-CHAR
001281r 3  FF 7F                .word $7FFF     ; MAX-N
001283r 3  FF FF                .word $FFFF     ; MAX-U
001285r 3  80 00                .word $0080     ; RETURN-STACK-CELLS
001287r 3  20 00                .word $0020     ; STACK-CELLS (from definitions.asm)
001289r 3  09 00                .word $0009     ; WORDLISTS
00128Br 3               
00128Br 3               env_results_double:
00128Br 3  FF 7F FF FF          .word $7FFF, $FFFF      ; MAX-D
00128Fr 3  FF FF FF FF          .word $FFFF, $FFFF      ; MAX-UD
001293r 3               
001293r 3               
001293r 3               ; ## EQUAL ( n n -- f ) "See if TOS and NOS are equal"
001293r 3               ; ## "="  auto  ANS core
001293r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Equal"""
001293r 3               
001293r 3               xt_equal:
001293r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
001296r 3               
001296r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x                 ; LSB
001298r 3  D5 02                        cmp 2,x
00129Ar 3  D0 0A                        bne @false
00129Cr 3               
00129Cr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x                 ; MSB
00129Er 3  D5 03                        cmp 3,x
0012A0r 3  D0 04                        bne @false
0012A2r 3               
0012A2r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$ff
0012A4r 3  80 02                        bra @done
0012A6r 3               
0012A6r 3  A9 00        @false:         lda #0                  ; drop thru to done
0012A8r 3               
0012A8r 3  95 02        @done:          sta 2,x
0012AAr 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
0012ACr 3               
0012ACr 3  E8                           inx
0012ADr 3  E8                           inx
0012AEr 3               
0012AEr 3  60           z_equal:        rts
0012AFr 3               
0012AFr 3               
0012AFr 3               
0012AFr 3               ; ## BLANK ( addr u -- ) "Fill memory region with spaces"
0012AFr 3               ; ## "blank"  auto  ANS string
0012AFr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/string/BLANK"""
0012AFr 3               xt_blank:
0012AFr 3                               ; We don't check for underflow here because
0012AFr 3                               ; we deal with that in FILL
0012AFr 3  CA                           dex
0012B0r 3  CA                           dex
0012B1r 3  A9 20                        lda #AscSP
0012B3r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0012B5r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
0012B7r 3               
0012B7r 3  80 06                        bra xt_fill     ; skip over code for ERASE
0012B9r 3               
0012B9r 3               
0012B9r 3               ; ## ERASE ( addr u -- ) "Fill memory region with zeros"
0012B9r 3               ; ## "erase"  auto  ANS core ext
0012B9r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ERASE
0012B9r 3                       ; Note that ERASE works with "address" units
0012B9r 3                       ; (bytes), not cells.
0012B9r 3                       ; """
0012B9r 3               
0012B9r 3               xt_erase:
0012B9r 3                               ; We don't check for underflow here because
0012B9r 3                               ; we deal with that in FILL
0012B9r 3  CA                           dex
0012BAr 3  CA                           dex
0012BBr 3  74 00                        stz 0,x
0012BDr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
0012BFr 3               
0012BFr 3                               ; fall through to FILL
0012BFr 3               
0012BFr 3               ; ## FILL ( addr u char -- ) "Fill a memory region with a character"
0012BFr 3               ; ## "fill"  auto  ANS core
0012BFr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/FILL
0012BFr 3                       ; Fill u bytes of memory with char starting at addr. Note that
0012BFr 3                       ; this works on bytes, not on cells. On an 8-bit machine such as the
0012BFr 3                       ; 65c02, this is a serious pain in the rear. It is not defined what
0012BFr 3                       ; happens when we reach the end of the address space
0012BFr 3                       ; """
0012BFr 3               xt_fill:
0012BFr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
0012C2r 3               
0012C2r 3                               ; We use tmp1 to hold the address
0012C2r 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x         ; LSB
0012C4r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
0012C6r 3  B5 05                        lda 5,x
0012C8r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
0012CAr 3               
0012CAr 3                               ; We use tmp2 to hold the counter
0012CAr 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
0012CCr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
0012CEr 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0012D0r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
0012D2r 3               
0012D2r 3                               ; We use Y to hold the character
0012D2r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0012D4r 3  A8                           tay
0012D5r 3               @loop:
0012D5r 3                               ; Unfortunately, we also need to make sure that we don't
0012D5r 3                               ; write further than the end of the RAM. So RAM_END must
0012D5r 3                               ; be larger or equal to the current address
0012D5r 3  A9 80                        lda #>ram_end           ; MSB
0012D7r 3  C5 rr                        cmp tmp1+1
0012D9r 3  90 21                        bcc @done               ; RAM_END < TMP1, so leave
0012DBr 3  D0 06                        bne @check_counter      ; RAM_END is not smaller and not equal
0012DDr 3               
0012DDr 3  A9 00                        lda #<ram_end           ; LSB, because MSBs were equal
0012DFr 3  C5 rr                        cmp tmp1
0012E1r 3  90 19                        bcc @done               ; RAM_END < TMP1, so leave
0012E3r 3               
0012E3r 3               @check_counter:
0012E3r 3                               ; See if our counter has reached zero
0012E3r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2
0012E5r 3  05 rr                        ora tmp2+1
0012E7r 3  F0 13                        beq @done
0012E9r 3               
0012E9r 3                               ; We're not in ROM and we still have stuff on the counter, so
0012E9r 3                               ; let's actually do what we came here to do
0012E9r 3  98                           tya
0012EAr 3  92 rr                        sta (tmp1)
0012ECr 3               
0012ECr 3                               ; Adjust the counter
0012ECr 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2
0012EEr 3  D0 02                        bne @1
0012F0r 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp2+1
0012F2r 3  C6 rr        @1:               dec tmp2
0012F4r 3               
0012F4r 3                               ; Next address
0012F4r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1
0012F6r 3  D0 DD                        bne @loop
0012F8r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1+1
0012FAr 3               
0012FAr 3  80 D9                        bra @loop
0012FCr 3               
0012FCr 3               @done:
0012FCr 3                               ; Drop three cells off the Data Stack. This uses one byte
0012FCr 3                               ; less than six times INX
0012FCr 3  8A                           txa
0012FDr 3  18                           clc
0012FEr 3  69 06                        adc #6
001300r 3  AA                           tax
001301r 3               z_blank:
001301r 3               z_erase:
001301r 3  60           z_fill:         rts
001302r 3               
001302r 3               
001302r 3               
001302r 3               ; ## EXECUTE ( xt -- ) "Jump to word based on execution token"
001302r 3               ; ## "execute"  auto  ANS core
001302r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/EXECUTE"""
001302r 3               xt_execute:
001302r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
001305r 3               
001305r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr doexecute   ; do not combine to JMP (native coding)
001308r 3               
001308r 3  60           z_execute:      rts
001309r 3               
001309r 3               doexecute:
001309r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
00130Br 3  85 rr                        sta ip
00130Dr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
00130Fr 3  85 rr                        sta ip+1
001311r 3               
001311r 3  E8                           inx
001312r 3  E8                           inx
001313r 3               
001313r 3                               ; we don't need a RTS here because we highjack the RTS of
001313r 3                               ; the word we're calling to get back to xt_execute
001313r 3  6C rr rr                     jmp (ip)
001316r 3               
001316r 3               ; end of doexecute
001316r 3               
001316r 3               
001316r 3               ; ## EXECUTE_PARSING ( addr u xt -- ) "Pass a string to a parsing word"
001316r 3               ; ## "execute-parsing"  auto  Gforth
001316r 3                       ; """https://www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/The-Input-Stream.html
001316r 3                       ; Execute the parsing word defined by the execution token (xt) on the
001316r 3                       ; string as if it were passed on the command line. See the file
001316r 3                       ; tests/tali.fs for examples.
001316r 3                       ;
001316r 3                       ; Note that this word is coded completely
001316r 3                       ; different in its Gforth version, see the file execute-parsing.fs
001316r 3                       ; (in /usr/share/gforth/0.7.3/compat/ on Ubuntu 18.04 LTS) for details.
001316r 3                       ; """
001316r 3               xt_execute_parsing:
001316r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
001319r 3               
001319r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_input_to_r       ; save normal input for later
00131Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_not_rote         ; -ROT ( xt addr u )
00131Fr 3               
00131Fr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x                 ; TOS is new ciblen
001321r 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen
001323r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
001325r 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen+1
001327r 3               
001327r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x                 ; NOS is new cib
001329r 3  85 rr                        sta cib
00132Br 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
00132Dr 3  85 rr                        sta cib+1
00132Fr 3               
00132Fr 3  64 rr                        stz toin                ; Set >IN to zero
001331r 3  64 rr                        stz toin+1
001333r 3               
001333r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_drop         ; 2DROP ( xt )
001336r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_execute
001339r 3               
001339r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_to_input
00133Cr 3               
00133Cr 3               z_execute_parsing:
00133Cr 3  60                           rts
00133Dr 3               
00133Dr 3               
00133Dr 3               ; ## EXIT ( -- ) "Return control to the calling word immediately"
00133Dr 3               ; ## "exit"  auto  ANS core
00133Dr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/EXIT
00133Dr 3                       ; If we're in a loop, we need to UNLOOP first and get everything
00133Dr 3                       ; we we might have put on the Return Stack off as well. This should
00133Dr 3                       ; be natively compiled.
00133Dr 3                       ; """
00133Dr 3               
00133Dr 3               xt_exit:
00133Dr 3  60                           rts             ; keep before z_exit
00133Er 3               z_exit:                         ; never reached
00133Er 3               
00133Er 3               
00133Er 3               
00133Er 3               ; ## FALSE ( -- f ) "Push flag FALSE to Data Stack"
00133Er 3               ; ## "false"  auto  ANS core ext
00133Er 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/FALSE"""
00133Er 3               xt_false:
00133Er 3  CA                           dex
00133Fr 3  CA                           dex
001340r 3  74 00                        stz 0,x
001342r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
001344r 3               
001344r 3  60           z_false:        rts
001345r 3               
001345r 3               
001345r 3               ; ## FETCH ( addr -- n ) "Push cell content from memory to stack"
001345r 3               ; ## "@"  auto  ANS core
001345r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Fetch"""
001345r 3               xt_fetch:
001345r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
001348r 3               
001348r 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)               ; LSB
00134Ar 3  A8                           tay
00134Br 3  F6 00                        inc 0,x
00134Dr 3  D0 02                        bne @1
00134Fr 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x
001351r 3               @1:
001351r 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)               ; MSB
001353r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001355r 3  94 00                        sty 0,x
001357r 3               
001357r 3  60           z_fetch:        rts
001358r 3               
001358r 3               
001358r 3               ; ## FIND ( caddr -- addr 0 | xt 1 | xt -1 ) "Find word in Dictionary"
001358r 3               ; ## "find"  auto  ANS core
001358r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/FIND
001358r 3                       ; Included for backwards compatibility only, because it still
001358r 3                       ; can be found in so may examples. It should, however, be replaced
001358r 3                       ; by FIND-NAME. Counted string either returns address with a FALSE
001358r 3                       ; flag if not found in the Dictionary, or the xt with a flag to
001358r 3                       ; indicate if this is immediate or not. FIND is a wrapper around
001358r 3                       ; FIND-NAME, we get this all over with as quickly as possible. See
001358r 3                       ; https://www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/Word-Lists.html
001358r 3                       ; https://www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/Name-token.html
001358r 3                       ; """
001358r 3               
001358r 3               xt_find:
001358r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
00135Br 3               
00135Br 3                               ; Save address in case conversion fails. We use the
00135Br 3                               ; Return Stack instead of temporary variables like TMP1
00135Br 3                               ; because this is shorter and anybody still using FIND
00135Br 3                               ; can't be worried about speed anyway
00135Br 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x                 ; MSB
00135Dr 3  48                           pha
00135Er 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x                 ; LSB
001360r 3  48                           pha
001361r 3               
001361r 3                               ; Convert ancient-type counted string address to
001361r 3                               ; modern format
001361r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_count            ; ( caddr -- addr u )
001364r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_find_name        ; ( addr u -- nt | 0 )
001367r 3               
001367r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001369r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
00136Br 3  D0 0B                        bne @found_word
00136Dr 3               
00136Dr 3                               ; No word found. Return address of the string and a false
00136Dr 3                               ; flag
00136Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_false            ; ( 0 0 )
001370r 3               
001370r 3                               ; The address needs to be restored.
001370r 3  68                           pla                     ; LSB of address
001371r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001373r 3  68                           pla
001374r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x                 ; MSB of address
001376r 3               
001376r 3  80 27                        bra @done               ; ( addr 0 )
001378r 3               
001378r 3               @found_word:
001378r 3                               ; We don't need the address after all, dump it
001378r 3  68                           pla
001379r 3  68                           pla
00137Ar 3               
00137Ar 3                               ; We arrive here with ( nt ) on the TOS. Now we have to
00137Ar 3                               ; convert the return values to FIND's format
00137Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dup              ; ( nt nt )
00137Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_name_to_int      ; ( nt xt )
001380r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_swap             ; ( xt nt )
001383r 3               
001383r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0                  ; Prepare flag
001385r 3               
001385r 3                               ; The flags are in the second byte of the header
001385r 3  F6 00                        inc 0,x
001387r 3  D0 02                        bne @1
001389r 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x                 ; ( xt nt+1 )
00138Br 3               @1:
00138Br 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)               ; ( xt char )
00138Dr 3  29 04                        and #IM
00138Fr 3  D0 08                        bne @immediate          ; bit set, we're immediate
001391r 3               
001391r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF                ; We're not immediate, return -1
001393r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001395r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001397r 3  80 06                        bra @done
001399r 3               
001399r 3               @immediate:
001399r 3  A9 01                        lda #1                  ; We're immediate, return 1
00139Br 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00139Dr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
00139Fr 3               @done:
00139Fr 3  60           z_find:         rts
0013A0r 3               
0013A0r 3               
0013A0r 3               
0013A0r 3               ; ## FIND_NAME ( addr u -- nt|0 ) "Get the name token of input word"
0013A0r 3               ; ## "find-name"  auto  Gforth
0013A0r 3               
0013A0r 3               xt_find_name:
0013A0r 3                       ; """www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/Name-token.html
0013A0r 3                       ; Given a string, find the Name Token (nt) of a word or return
0013A0r 3                       ; zero if the word is not in the dictionary. We use this instead of
0013A0r 3                       ; ancient FIND to look up words in the Dictionary passed by
0013A0r 3                       ; PARSE-NAME. Note this returns the nt, not the xt of a word like
0013A0r 3                       ; FIND. To convert, use NAME>INT. This is a Gforth word. See
0013A0r 3                       ; https://www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/Name-token.html
0013A0r 3                       ; FIND calls this word
0013A0r 3                       ; """
0013A0r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
0013A3r 3               
0013A3r 3                               ; check for special case of an empty string (length zero)
0013A3r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0013A5r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
0013A7r 3  D0 03                        bne @nonempty
0013A9r 3               
0013A9r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @fail_done
0013ACr 3               
0013ACr 3               @nonempty:
0013ACr 3                               ; Set up for traversing the wordlist search order.
0013ACr 3  64 rr                        stz tmp3                ; Start at the beginning
0013AEr 3               
0013AEr 3               @wordlist_loop:
0013AEr 3  A0 1E                        ldy #num_order_offset   ; Compare to byte variable #ORDER
0013B0r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp3
0013B2r 3  D1 rr                        cmp (up),y              ; Check to see if we are done
0013B4r 3  D0 03                        bne @have_string
0013B6r 3               
0013B6r 3                               ; We ran out of wordlists to search.
0013B6r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @fail_done
0013B9r 3               
0013B9r 3               @have_string:
0013B9r 3                               ; set up first loop iteration
0013B9r 3               
0013B9r 3                               ; Get the current wordlist id
0013B9r 3  18                           clc             ; SEARCH-ORDER is array of bytes.
0013BAr 3  69 1F                        adc #search_order_offset
0013BCr 3  A8                           tay
0013BDr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y      ; Get the id byte, which is the offset
0013BFr 3                                               ; into the cell array WORDLISTS
0013BFr 3               
0013BFr 3                               ; Get the DP for that wordlist.
0013BFr 3  0A                           asl                     ; Turn offset into cells offset.
0013C0r 3  18                           clc
0013C1r 3  69 06                        adc #wordlists_offset
0013C3r 3  A8                           tay
0013C4r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0013C6r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
0013C8r 3  C8                           iny
0013C9r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0013CBr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
0013CDr 3               
0013CDr 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x                 ; Address of mystery string
0013CFr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
0013D1r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0013D3r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
0013D5r 3               
0013D5r 3               @loop:
0013D5r 3                               ; first quick test: Are strings the same length?
0013D5r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)
0013D7r 3  D5 00                        cmp 0,x
0013D9r 3  D0 54                        bne @next_entry
0013DBr 3               
0013DBr 3               @compare_string:
0013DBr 3                               ; are the same length, so we now have to compare each
0013DBr 3                               ; character
0013DBr 3               
0013DBr 3                               ; second quick test: Is the first character the same?
0013DBr 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp2)      ; first character of mystery string
0013DDr 3               
0013DDr 3                               ; Lowercase the incoming charcter.
0013DDr 3  C9 5B                        cmp #$5B        ; ASCII '[' (one past Z)
0013DFr 3  B0 07                        bcs @compare_first
0013E1r 3  C9 41                        cmp #$41        ; ASCII 'A'
0013E3r 3  90 03                        bcc @compare_first
0013E5r 3               
0013E5r 3                               ; An uppercase letter has been located.  Make it
0013E5r 3                               ; lowercase.
0013E5r 3  18                           clc
0013E6r 3  69 20                        adc #$20
0013E8r 3               
0013E8r 3               @compare_first:
0013E8r 3  A0 08                        ldy #8          ; Offset in nt to name
0013EAr 3  D1 rr                        cmp (tmp1),y    ; first character of current word
0013ECr 3  D0 41                        bne @next_entry
0013EEr 3               
0013EEr 3                               ; String length is the same and the first character is the
0013EEr 3                               ; same. If the length of the string is 1, we're already done
0013EEr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0013F0r 3  3A                           dec
0013F1r 3  F0 2C                        beq @success
0013F3r 3               
0013F3r 3                               ; No such luck: The strings are the same length and the first
0013F3r 3                               ; char is the same, but the word is more than one char long.
0013F3r 3                               ; So we suck it up and compare every single character. We go
0013F3r 3                               ; from back to front, because words like CELLS and CELL+ would
0013F3r 3                               ; take longer otherwise. We can also shorten the loop by one
0013F3r 3                               ; because we've already compared the first char.
0013F3r 3               
0013F3r 3                               ; The string of the word we're testing against is 8 bytes down
0013F3r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1
0013F5r 3  48                           pha             ; Preserve tmp1 on the return stack.
0013F6r 3  18                           clc
0013F7r 3  69 08                        adc #8
0013F9r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1        ; Reusing tmp1 temporarily for string check.
0013FBr 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1+1
0013FDr 3  48                           pha             ; Preserve tmp1+1 on the return stack.
0013FEr 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; we only need the carry
001400r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
001402r 3               
001402r 3  B4 00                        ldy 0,x         ; index is length of string minus 1
001404r 3  88                           dey
001405r 3               
001405r 3               @string_loop:
001405r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp2),y    ; last char of mystery string
001407r 3               
001407r 3                               ; Lowercase the incoming charcter.
001407r 3  C9 5B                        cmp #$5B         ; ASCII '[' (one past Z)
001409r 3  B0 07                        bcs @check_char
00140Br 3  C9 41                        cmp #$41        ; ASCII 'A'
00140Dr 3  90 03                        bcc @check_char
00140Fr 3               
00140Fr 3                               ; An uppercase letter has been located.  Make it
00140Fr 3                               ; lowercase.
00140Fr 3  18                           clc
001410r 3  69 20                        adc #$20
001412r 3               
001412r 3               @check_char:
001412r 3  D1 rr                        cmp (tmp1),y    ; last char of word we're testing against
001414r 3  D0 13                        bne @next_entry_tmp1
001416r 3               
001416r 3  88                           dey
001417r 3  D0 EC                        bne @string_loop
001419r 3               
001419r 3               @success_tmp1:
001419r 3  68                           pla             ; Restore tmp1 from the return stack.
00141Ar 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
00141Cr 3  68                           pla
00141Dr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00141Fr 3               
00141Fr 3               @success:
00141Fr 3                               ; The strings match. Put correct nt NOS, because we'll drop
00141Fr 3                               ; TOS before we leave
00141Fr 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1
001421r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001423r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1+1
001425r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
001427r 3               
001427r 3  80 20                        bra @done
001429r 3               
001429r 3               @next_entry_tmp1:
001429r 3  68                           pla             ; Restore tmp1 from the return stack.
00142Ar 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
00142Cr 3  68                           pla
00142Dr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00142Fr 3               
00142Fr 3               @next_entry:
00142Fr 3                               ; Not the same, so we get the next word. Next header
00142Fr 3                               ; address is two bytes down
00142Fr 3  A0 02                        ldy #2
001431r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
001433r 3  48                           pha
001434r 3  C8                           iny
001435r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
001437r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
001439r 3  68                           pla
00143Ar 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00143Cr 3               
00143Cr 3                               ; If we got a zero, we've walked the whole Dictionary and
00143Cr 3                               ; return as a failure, otherwise try again
00143Cr 3  05 rr                        ora tmp1+1
00143Er 3  D0 95                        bne @loop
001440r 3               
001440r 3                               ; Move on to the next wordlist in the search order.
001440r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp3
001442r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @wordlist_loop
001445r 3               
001445r 3               @fail_done:
001445r 3  74 02                        stz 2,x         ; failure flag
001447r 3  74 03                        stz 3,x
001449r 3               @done:
001449r 3  E8                           inx
00144Ar 3  E8                           inx
00144Br 3               
00144Br 3  60           z_find_name:    rts
00144Cr 3               
00144Cr 3               
00144Cr 3               
00144Cr 3               ; ## FLUSH ( -- ) "Save dirty buffers and empty buffers"
00144Cr 3               ; ## "flush"  auto  ANS block
00144Cr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/FLUSH"""
00144Cr 3               xt_flush:
00144Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_save_buffers
00144Fr 3               
00144Fr 3                               ; Set the buffer status to empty.
00144Fr 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
001451r 3  A9 00                        lda #0
001453r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y      ; Only LSB is used.
001455r 3               z_flush:
001455r 3  60                           rts
001456r 3               
001456r 3               
001456r 3               ; ## FM_SLASH_MOD ( d n1  -- rem n2 ) "Floored signed division"
001456r 3               ; ## "fm/mod"  auto  ANS core
001456r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/FMDivMOD
001456r 3                       ; Note that by default, Tali Forth uses SM/REM for most things.
001456r 3                       ;
001456r 3                       ; There are various ways to realize this. We follow EForth with
001456r 3                       ;    DUP 0< DUP >R  IF NEGATE >R DNEGATE R> THEN >R DUP
001456r 3                       ;    0<  IF R@ + THEN  R> UM/MOD R> IF SWAP NEGATE SWAP THEN
001456r 3                       ; See (http://www.forth.org/eforth.html). However you can also
001456r 3                       ; go FM/MOD via SM/REM (http://www.figuk.plus.com/build/arith.htm):
001456r 3                       ;     DUP >R  SM/REM DUP 0< IF SWAP R> + SWAP 1+ ELSE  R> DROP THEN
001456r 3                       ; """
001456r 3               
001456r 3               xt_fm_slash_mod:
001456r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
001459r 3               
001459r 3                               ; if sign of n1 is negative, negate both n1 and d
001459r 3  64 rr                        stz tmp2        ; default: n is positive
00145Br 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x         ; MSB of n1
00145Dr 3  10 0E                        bpl @check_d
00145Fr 3               
00145Fr 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2        ; set flag to negative for n1
001461r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_negate   ; NEGATE
001464r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_to_r     ; >R
001467r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dnegate  ; DNEGATE
00146Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_from   ; R>
00146Dr 3               
00146Dr 3               @check_d:
00146Dr 3                               ; If d is negative, add n1 to high cell of d
00146Dr 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x         ; MSB of high word of d
00146Fr 3  10 0D                        bpl @multiply
001471r 3               
001471r 3  18                           clc
001472r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x         ; LSB of n1
001474r 3  75 02                        adc 2,x         ; LSB of dh
001476r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001478r 3               
001478r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x         ; MSB of n1
00147Ar 3  75 03                        adc 3,x         ; MSB of dh
00147Cr 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
00147Er 3               
00147Er 3               @multiply:
00147Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_um_slash_mod     ; ( d n1 -- rem n2 )
001481r 3               
001481r 3                               ; if n was negative, negate the result
001481r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2
001483r 3  F0 07                        beq @done
001485r 3               
001485r 3  E8                           inx             ; pretend that we SWAP
001486r 3  E8                           inx
001487r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_negate
00148Ar 3  CA                           dex
00148Br 3  CA                           dex
00148Cr 3               @done:
00148Cr 3  60           z_fm_slash_mod: rts
00148Dr 3               
00148Dr 3               
00148Dr 3               
00148Dr 3               ; ## FORTH ( -- ) "Replace first WID in search order with Forth-Wordlist"
00148Dr 3               ; ## "forth"  auto  ANS search ext
00148Dr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/FORTH"""
00148Dr 3               xt_forth:
00148Dr 3  A0 1F                        ldy #search_order_offset
00148Fr 3  A9 00                        lda #0          ; The WID for Forth is 0.
001491r 3               
001491r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
001493r 3               z_forth:
001493r 3  60                           rts
001494r 3               
001494r 3               
001494r 3               ; This is a special jsr target to skip the zeroing of BLK at the beginning
001494r 3               ; of evaluate.  It's used by LOAD to allow setting BLK while the block is
001494r 3               ; being evaluated.  Evaluate's normal behavior is to zero BLK.
001494r 3               load_evaluate:
001494r 3                               ; Set a flag (using tmp1) to not zero BLK
001494r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF
001496r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
001498r 3  80 11                        bra load_evaluate_start
00149Ar 3               
00149Ar 3               ; ## EVALUATE ( addr u -- ) "Execute a string"
00149Ar 3               ; ## "evaluate"  auto  ANS core
00149Ar 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/EVALUATE
00149Ar 3                       ; Set SOURCE-ID to -1, make addr u the input source, set >IN to zero.
00149Ar 3                       ; After processing the line, revert to old input source. We use this
00149Ar 3                       ; to compile high-level Forth words and user-defined words during
00149Ar 3                       ; start up and cold boot. In contrast to ACCEPT, we need to, uh,
00149Ar 3                       ; accept more than 255 characters here, even though it's a pain in
00149Ar 3                       ; the 8-bit.
00149Ar 3                       ; """
00149Ar 3               
00149Ar 3               xt_evaluate:
00149Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
00149Dr 3               
00149Dr 3                               ; Clear the flag to zero BLK.  Only LOAD will set the flag,
00149Dr 3                               ; and will set the block number.
00149Dr 3  64 rr                        stz tmp1
00149Fr 3               
00149Fr 3                               ; If u is zero (which can happen a lot for the user-defined
00149Fr 3                               ; words), just leave again
00149Fr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0014A1r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
0014A3r 3  D0 06                        bne _eval_got_work
0014A5r 3               
0014A5r 3  E8                           inx
0014A6r 3  E8                           inx
0014A7r 3  E8                           inx
0014A8r 3  E8                           inx
0014A9r 3               
0014A9r 3  80 42                        bra _eval_done
0014ABr 3               
0014ABr 3               ; Special entry point for LOAD to bypass the zeroing of BLK.
0014ABr 3               load_evaluate_start:
0014ABr 3               _eval_got_work:
0014ABr 3                               ; Save the current value of BLK on the return stack.
0014ABr 3  A0 01                        ldy #blk_offset+1
0014ADr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0014AFr 3  48                           pha
0014B0r 3  88                           dey
0014B1r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0014B3r 3  48                           pha
0014B4r 3               
0014B4r 3                               ; See if we should zero BLK.
0014B4r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1
0014B6r 3  D0 05                        bne @nozero
0014B8r 3               
0014B8r 3                               ; Set BLK to zero.
0014B8r 3                               ; lda #0        ; A is already zero from loading tmp1
0014B8r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0014BAr 3  C8                           iny
0014BBr 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0014BDr 3               
0014BDr 3               @nozero:
0014BDr 3                               ; Save the input state to the Return Stack
0014BDr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_input_to_r
0014C0r 3               
0014C0r 3                               ; set SOURCE-ID to -1
0014C0r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$ff
0014C2r 3  85 rr                        sta insrc
0014C4r 3  85 rr                        sta insrc+1
0014C6r 3               
0014C6r 3                               ; set >IN to zero
0014C6r 3  64 rr                        stz toin
0014C8r 3  64 rr                        stz toin+1
0014CAr 3               
0014CAr 3                               ; move TOS and NOS to input buffers
0014CAr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0014CCr 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen
0014CEr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
0014D0r 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen+1
0014D2r 3               
0014D2r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
0014D4r 3  85 rr                        sta cib
0014D6r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0014D8r 3  85 rr                        sta cib+1
0014DAr 3               
0014DAr 3  E8                           inx             ; A clean stack is a clean mind
0014DBr 3  E8                           inx
0014DCr 3  E8                           inx
0014DDr 3  E8                           inx
0014DEr 3               
0014DEr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr interpret   ; ( -- )
0014E1r 3               
0014E1r 3                               ; restore variables
0014E1r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_to_input
0014E4r 3               
0014E4r 3                               ; Restore BLK from the return stack.
0014E4r 3  A0 00                        ldy #blk_offset
0014E6r 3  68                           pla
0014E7r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0014E9r 3  C8                           iny
0014EAr 3  68                           pla
0014EBr 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0014EDr 3               
0014EDr 3               _eval_done:
0014EDr 3  60           z_evaluate:     rts
0014EEr 3               
0014EEr 3               
0014EEr 3               
0014EEr 3               ; ## FORTH_WORDLIST ( -- u ) "WID for the Forth Wordlist"
0014EEr 3               ; ## "forth-wordlist"  auto  ANS search
0014EEr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/FORTH-WORDLIST"""
0014EEr 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the actual code is shared with ZERO.
0014EEr 3               
0014EEr 3               
0014EEr 3               ; ## GET_CURRENT ( -- wid ) "Get the id of the compilation wordlist"
0014EEr 3               ; ## "get-current" auto ANS search
0014EEr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/GET-CURRENT"""
0014EEr 3               
0014EEr 3               xt_get_current:
0014EEr 3                               ; This is a little different than some of the variables
0014EEr 3                               ; in the user area as we want the value rather than
0014EEr 3                               ; the address.
0014EEr 3  CA                           dex
0014EFr 3  CA                           dex
0014F0r 3  A0 04                        ldy #current_offset
0014F2r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0014F4r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x         ; CURRENT is a byte variable
0014F6r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; so the MSB is zero.
0014F8r 3               
0014F8r 3  60           z_get_current:  rts
0014F9r 3               
0014F9r 3               
0014F9r 3               
0014F9r 3               ; ## GET_ORDER ( -- wid_n .. wid_1 n) "Get the current search order"
0014F9r 3               ; ## "get-order" auto ANS search
0014F9r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/GET-ORDER"""
0014F9r 3               
0014F9r 3               xt_get_order:
0014F9r 3                               ; Get #ORDER - the number of wordlists in the search order.
0014F9r 3  A0 1E                        ldy #num_order_offset
0014FBr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0014FDr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
0014FFr 3  F0 16                        beq @done       ; If zero, there are no wordlists.
001501r 3               
001501r 3               @loop:
001501r 3                               ; Count down towards the front of the list.
001501r 3                               ; By decrementing first, we also turn the length into an offset.
001501r 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp1        ; Count down by bytes.
001503r 3               
001503r 3                               ; Get a pointer to the current wordlist, working back to front.
001503r 3  A9 1F                        lda #search_order_offset
001505r 3  18                           clc
001506r 3  65 rr                        adc tmp1
001508r 3  A8                           tay
001509r 3               
001509r 3                               ; Put that wordlist id on the stack.
001509r 3  CA                           dex
00150Ar 3  CA                           dex
00150Br 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00150Dr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x         ; Search order array is bytes, so
00150Fr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; put a zero in the high byte.
001511r 3               
001511r 3                               ; See if that was the last one to process (first in the list).
001511r 3  A9 00                        lda #0
001513r 3  C5 rr                        cmp tmp1
001515r 3  D0 EA                        bne @loop
001517r 3               
001517r 3               @done:
001517r 3                               ; Put the number of items on the stack.
001517r 3  CA                           dex
001518r 3  CA                           dex
001519r 3  A0 1E                        ldy #num_order_offset
00151Br 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00151Dr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00151Fr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; We only support 8 wordlists.
001521r 3               
001521r 3  60           z_get_order:    rts
001522r 3               
001522r 3               
001522r 3               
001522r 3               ; ## GREATER_THAN ( n n -- f ) "See if NOS is greater than TOS"
001522r 3               ; ## ">"  auto  ANS core
001522r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/more"""
001522r 3               
001522r 3               xt_greater_than:
001522r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
001525r 3               
001525r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0          ; default false
001527r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr compare_16bit
00152Ar 3               
00152Ar 3                               ; for signed numbers, NOS>TOS gives us Z=0 and N=1
00152Ar 3  F0 03                        beq @false
00152Cr 3  10 01                        bpl @false
00152Er 3               
00152Er 3                               ; true
00152Er 3  88                           dey
00152Fr 3               @false:
00152Fr 3  98                           tya
001530r 3               
001530r 3  E8                           inx
001531r 3  E8                           inx
001532r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001534r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001536r 3               
001536r 3  60           z_greater_than: rts
001537r 3               
001537r 3               
001537r 3               
001537r 3               ; ## HERE ( -- addr ) "Put Compiler Pointer on Data Stack"
001537r 3               ; ## "here"  auto  ANS core
001537r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/HERE
001537r 3                       ; This code is also used by the assembler directive ARROW
001537r 3                       ; ("->") though as immediate"""
001537r 3               xt_here:
001537r 3               xt_asm_arrow:
001537r 3  CA                           dex
001538r 3  CA                           dex
001539r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
00153Br 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00153Dr 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
00153Fr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001541r 3               
001541r 3               z_asm_arrow:
001541r 3  60           z_here:         rts

001542r 3               ; ## HEX ( -- ) "Change base radix to hexadecimal"
001542r 3               ; ## "hex"  auto  ANS core ext
001542r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/HEX"""
001542r 3               xt_hex:
001542r 3  A9 10                        lda #16
001544r 3  85 rr                        sta base
001546r 3  64 rr                        stz base+1              ; paranoid
001548r 3

001549r 3               
001549r 3               
001549r 3               ; ## HEXSTORE ( addr1 u1 addr2 -- u2 ) "Store a list of numbers"
001549r 3               ; ## "hexstore"  auto  Tali
001549r 3                       ; """Given a string addr1 u1 with numbers in the current base seperated
001549r 3                       ; by spaces, store the numbers at the address addr2, returning the
001549r 3                       ; number of elements. Non-number elements are skipped, an zero-length
001549r 3                       ; string produces a zero output.
001549r 3                       ; """
001549r 3               
001549r 3               xt_hexstore:
001549r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
00154Cr 3               
00154Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dup              ; Save copy of original address
00154Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_to_r         ; ( addr1 u1 ) ( R: addr2 addr2 )
001552r 3               
001552r 3               @loop:
001552r 3                               ; Loop until string is totally consumed
001552r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001554r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
001556r 3  F0 36                        beq @done
001558r 3               
001558r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_cleave           ; ( addr1 u1 addr3 u3 ) ( R: addr2 addr2 )
00155Br 3               
00155Br 3                               ; Prepare the conversion of the number.
00155Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_to_r
00155Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_zero
001561r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_zero
001564r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_r_from       ; ( addr1 u1 0 0 addr3 u3 ) ( R: addr2 addr2 )
001567r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_to_number        ; ( addr1 u1 n n addr4 u4 ) ( R: addr2 addr2 )
00156Ar 3               
00156Ar 3                               ; If u4 is not zero, we have leftover chars and have to do
00156Ar 3                               ; things differently
00156Ar 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
00156Cr 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
00156Er 3  D0 17                        bne @have_chars_left
001570r 3               
001570r 3                               ; Normal case, this number is all done
001570r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_drop         ; ( addr1 u1 n n ) ( R: addr2 addr2 )
001573r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_d_to_s           ; ( addr1 u1 n ) ( R: addr2 addr2 )
001576r 3               
001576r 3                               ; Store the new value
001576r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_fetch          ; ( addr1 u1 n addr2 ) ( R: addr2 addr2 )
001579r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_c_store          ; ( addr1 u1 ) ( R: addr2 addr2 )
00157Cr 3               
00157Cr 3                               ; Increase counter
00157Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_from           ; R>
00157Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_one_plus         ; 1+
001582r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_to_r             ; >R ( addr1 u1 ) ( R: addr2+1 addr2 )
001585r 3  80 CB                        bra @loop
001587r 3               
001587r 3               @have_chars_left:
